TD 

 
   Discontinuation of the stabilisation period of Next Games' IPO 
 
   NOT FOR RELEASE, PUBLICATION OR DISTRIBUTION, DIRECTLY OR INDIRECTLY, IN 
OR INTO THE UNITED STATES, CANADA, AUSTRALIA, HONG KONG, SOUTH AFRICA, 
SINGAPORE OR JAPAN OR ANY OTHER JURISDICTION IN WHICH THE DISTRIBUTION 
OR RELEASE WOULD BE UNLAWFUL. 
 
   Danske Bank A/S, Helsinki Branch ("Danske Bank"), the lead manager in 
the initial public offering of Next Games Corporation ("Next Games" or 
the "Company") states that no stabilisation measures have been carried 
out since the listing and that due to Next Games' share price 
development, Danske Bank has discontinued the stabilisation period. 
Therefore, Danske Bank will not use the put option, which allows Danske 
Bank to sell over-allotment shares to the Company. Next Games listed on 
the Nasdaq First North Finland marketplace maintained by Nasdaq Helsinki 
Ltd on 23 March 2017. 
 
   The size of the offering is confirmed at 4,376,530 shares and the gross 
proceeds from the offering are approximately EUR 32.8 million. 
 
   Further enquiries 
 
   Saara Bergström, CMO, Next Games Oyj, tel. +358 (0)50 483 3896, 
press@nextgames.com 
 
   About Next Games 
 
   Next Games is a mobile game developer and publisher specializing in 
service-based games based on entertainment franchises, such as movies, 
TV series or books. The developers of the critically acclaimed The 
Walking Dead: No Man's Land, redefines the way franchise entertainment 
transforms into highly engaging mobile games. The Walking Dead: No Man's 
Land, based on the popular AMC TV series, has been downloaded 16 million 
times. Next Games employs 70 people and is based in Helsinki, Finland. 
www.nextgames.com[http://www.nextgames.com]

HD  SEB Banka and Latvian branch of Danske Bank lend EUR 50.4 million to Valmieras Stikla Skiedra
BY LETA
WC 400 words
PD 3 April 2017
ET 03:15
SN Latvian News Agency
SC LETA
LA English
CY (c) 2017 LETA .

LP 

RIGA, April 3 (LETA) - SEB Banka and Latvian branch of Danske Bank will grant a EUR 50.4 million loan to Valmieras Stikla Skiedra fiberglass manufacturer for the expansion of its plant in the U.S., Valmieras Stikla Skiedra said in a statement to the Nasdaq Riga stock exchange. The company’s representatives informed that last Thursday, March 30, Valmieras Stikla Skiedra concluded a loan agreement with SEB Banka and the Latvian branch of Danske Bank to take a EUR 50.4 million loan for the expansion of the Valmieras Stikla Skiedra plant in the U.S.The Latvian fiberglass producer intends to use the financing to construct a fiberglass production (furnace) and fiberglass processing plant in the U.S.

TD 

The expansion will make it possible to increase the total production capacity of Valmiera Glass Group and its competitiveness in international markets, to achieve even better production stability and to react better to the growing market demand for fiberglass products.“Having built the fifth glass melting furnace of the group, with the planned production capacity of 50,000 tons of dry thread per year, the group’s total production capacity will grow. This is a good cornerstone for further successful development of the group,” said Valmieras Stikla Skiedra CEO Andre Schwiontek.It is planned that Valmieras Stikla SKiedra will repay the loan by March 2024, starting from 1 October 2018. The loan agreement is secured by all the companies of the group.Valmieras Stikla Skiedra established its U.S. subsidiary, P-D Valmiera Glass USA Corp, in 2014. At present, work is under way on its expansion, which envisages construction of a modern fiberglass production plant. The project is scheduled for completion in November 2017. According to preliminary data, Valmieras Stikla Skiedra closed 2016 with EUR 124.255 turnover, up 2.5 percent against 2015, and the group's profit contracted 7.1 percent to EUR 5.088 million.Valmiera Glass Group comprises parent company Valmieras Stikla Skiedra and its three subsidiaries: Valmiera Glass UK Ltd. in the United Kingdom, Valmiera Glass USA Corp. and Valmiera Glass USA Trading Corp. in the United States.Valmieras Stikla Skiedra shares are quoted on the Secondary List of the Nasdaq Riga stock exchange. The company's largest shareholders are P-D Glasseiden Oschatz GmbH and Vitrulan International GmbH.

SE Economy
HD Quick Hits: Reducing Debt Levels and Financial Risks in China; Danske Bank expects Sweden's central bank to announce it won't extend its QE program
BY By WSJ Staff
WC 905 words
PD 24 April 2017
ET 12:50
SN WSJ Pro Central Banking
SC RSTPROCB
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

The People's Bank of China said the nation could see more government measures to reduce debt, day-to-day operations at the Federal Reserve likely wouldn't be affected by a U.S. government shutdown, and Sweden's central bank will take center stage in Scandinavia this week. Here are quick hits on central banking and related market views from around the world.

China May Introduce More Deleveraging Measures

TD 

China likely will introduce more measures to cut down on debt, according to a newspaper from the People's Bank of China. "One can expect the roll of initiatives related to encouraging deleveraging in the financial sector to lead to deleveraging in the economy," said an editorial in Financial News. It said that while the economy has slowed, some funds have "diverged from reality," circulating among financial institutions and giving rise to "money chasing money." There, some financial institutions have increased the cost of capital by encouraging funds to circulate aimlessly within the financial system. The editorial didn't specify what measures may come. Chinese financial regulators have been on a tightening streak, with the central bank raising borrowing costs in the money market and trying to rein in speculative activity among banks.

Chao Deng

PBOC Chief: China Wants to Resolve Risks

People's Bank of China Gov. Zhou Xiaochuan stressed Beijing's efforts to keep rising financial risks in check during the weekend's IMF meetings in Washington. The "Chinese government attaches great importance to financial risks and is proactively taking actions to resolve the risks," he said in a statement posted on the central bank's website Sunday. The PBOC will continue using different monetary tools to keep liquidity at a largely steady level this year, state media cited him as saying.

Liyan Qi

China's Regulatory Tightening Won't Slow Economic Growth

China financial regulators' latest risk-control campaign has dampened sentiment in domestic bond and stock markets, but won't hurt economic growth, CICC said. That's because different regulators have learned to coordinate their actions better to fight speculation and the central bank would inject liquidity to avoid a "cash crunch" in the financial market if necessary, CICC said. China's economic recovery may last longer than some expected, it added.

Liyan Qi

What Would a Government Shutdown Mean for the Fed?

If the U.S. government fails to avert a shutdown in the coming days, expect the Federal Reserve to remain open and its roughly 22,000 employees to keep coming to work regardless. Like the U.S. Postal Service, the Fed is an independent agency with its own sources of funding. The Fed's revenue is largely derived from interest on its large portfolio of bonds and other assets. After covering its operating and other expenses, the rest of the Fed's earnings are sent to the Treasury to help pay the federal government's bills. While a potential government shutdown is unlikely to affect the Fed's day-to-day operations, it could affect officials' views on the economy as they set monetary policy. The government shutdown in 2013 took a toll on economic growth by denting some measures of the labor market and federal spending.

Harriet Torry

Singapore Central Bank See Little Demand-Pulled Inflation

Singapore's inflation rate is projected to pick up this year, but it has more to do with the external price environment than any heating up of the local economy. The central bank said that "the projected pickup in inflation can be attributed to" higher energy and administrative prices "rather than generalized demand-induced price pressures." That vindicated this month's decision to stand pat on interest rates. The overall and core consumer price indexes rose 0.7% and 1.2%, respectively, in March, steady with February's levels. CPI fell an average rate 0.5% in 2016.

Gaurav Raghuvanshi

Riksbank to Take Center Stage in Scandinavia This Week

Thursday's Riksbank meeting will take center stage in Scandinavia this week. Danske Bank expects the Swedish central bank to announce that it won't extend its quantitative-easing program, which expires at the end of June, while flattening the repo path and postponing the first rate increase by another quarter or two. Danske still expects EUR/SEK to move slowly and gradually lower over the forecast horizon as valuation and relatively strong fundamentals kick in, targeting 9.30 and 9.20 in six months and 12 months, respectively. "However, we would wait to enter/add to short positions until after the Riksbank meeting though, as we could actually see even better levels ahead."

Dominic Chopping

Credit Focus to Switch From France to ECB, Rocking High Grade

Now that centrist Emmanuel Macron looks poised to become the next president of France, credit investors' focus should turn to the potential tapering of the European Central Bank's QE program, J.P. Morgan said. Higher government bond yields and increased volatility on the back of this should be negative for investment-grade corporate bonds. And while rising rates tend to affect speculative-grade names less, they could reverse search-for-yield dynamics.

Tasos Vossos

(The items in this column come from Market Talk, a feature of Dow Jones Newswires [https://www.dowjones.com/products/newswires/] that provides real-time analysis of news developments and market activity.)

HD  Danske Bank Oyj Danske Bank Plc Group's Interim Report January - March 2017
WC 1159 words
PD 28 April 2017
ET 01:40
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

 
TIDM89KN 
 
 
   Danske Bank Plc Group's Interim Report January - March 2017 
 
   Good start to the year 
 
   The Finnish economy continued to improve in the first months of 2017, 
and positive signals could be seen in the latest economic indicators. 
The uptick in economic confidence was reflected in increased demand for 
lending among personal customers as well as in signs of improved 
economic activity among corporate customers. Total income for Danske 
Bank's operations in Finland[1] for January - March 2017 amounted to EUR 
169.4 million (EUR 154.1 million in Q1 2016), up 10% compared to 
previous year. 
 
   Despite continued low interest rate environment, net interest income for 
the period increased 10%, driven by lower funding costs, increase in 
lending and adjustments in deposit rates. Net fee income decreased by 
3%. Net trading income was positively affected by valuation adjustments 
on derivatives (xVA). Operating expenses were flat, and profit before 
taxes increased by 31% to EUR 81.8 million. 
 
   "In the first quarter of 2017, we saw a positive effect from valuation 
adjustments and lower funding costs. Our core business continued to 
perform solidly, however, and lending to small and medium sized 
corporate customers increased by 5%. We saw an especially strong demand 
for asset finance solutions, which seems to indicate a recovery in 
companies' willingness to invest. Consumer interest in mortgages was 
record high, and the volume of new granted mortgages grew by 13% 
compared to previous year. I am especially happy that our efforts to 
encourage first home buyers were reflected in a 29% growth in new first 
home mortgages," says Risto Tornivaara, CEO of Danske Bank Plc. 
 
   Financial Highlights of Danske Bank's operations in Finland 
 
   In addition to Danske Bank Plc, Danske Bank's operations in Finland 
include the Helsinki branch of Danske Bank A/S.

   Outlook for 2017 
 
   Growth in Finnish economy is expected to remain moderate in 2017-2018 
and the interest environment, especially short-term interest rates, is 
expected to remain at low level also during 2017. 
 
   We expect our lending to personal and corporate customers to continue 
growing in 2017 and thus we anticipate that our net interest income and 
total income will be higher compared to 2016. 
 
   Operating expenses are expected to be slightly lower than previous year 
since the Bank continues to have a strong focus on improving our cost 
efficiency and operational processes. Overall, we expect that our net 
profit for 2017 will be slightly higher than 2016. 
 
   Possible merging of activities in Finland 
 
   As announced on February 2, 2017, the Danske Bank Group is looking into 
the possibilities of merging its activities in Finland - Danske Bank Plc 
and Danske Bank A/S, Helsinki branch - into a single branch. In doing so, 
the Danske Bank Group would achieve a uniform organisational structure 
across the Nordic markets. The change would be primarily of a technical 
nature and would not change the way in which we serve our customers, nor 
would employees experience changes. 
 
   As a part of this process, the Board of Directors of Danske Bank Plc 
approved on March 23, 2017 a plan aiming at separating the bank's 
mortgage credit banking business by way of a partial demerger. The 
planned de-merger has no effects on Danske Bank Plc's customers. 
 
   The demerger is subject to approval by the general meeting of Danske 
Bank Plc and the acquiring company obtaining necessary licenses to 
operate as a Finnish credit institution and mortgage credit bank. 
Application for such licenses has been filed with the Finnish Financial 
Supervisory Authority. 
 
   Interim report for January-June 2017 
 
   Danske Bank Plc Group publishes only one interim report during 2017. The 
Interim Report January - June 2017 will be released on 20 July 2017. 
 
   For further information: 
 
   Risto Tornivaara, CEO of Danske Bank Plc, tel. +358 (0)10 546 6675 
 
   Danske Bank is Finland's third largest bank, which serves around a 
million Finnish personal, business and institutional customers. Danske 
Bank Plc is a part of the Nordic Danske Bank Group. 
 
   Danske Bank is a Nordic universal bank with strong regional roots and 
bridges to the rest of the world. We serve more than 3.4 million 
personal, business and institutional customers, and in addition to 
banking services, we offer life insurance and pension, mortgage credit, 
wealth management, real estate and leasing services and products. 
 
   Our vision is to be recognised as the most trusted financial partner. We 
are driven by a desire to make important financial decisions and daily 
banking easy, and our aim is to create long-term value for our customers 
and investors and the societies we are a part of. 
 
   Danske Bank is headquartered in Copenhagen and is listed on Nasdaq 
Copenhagen.

HD Danske Bank Lithuania's Q1 net profit from core activities down 24 pct to EUR 2.5 mln y/y
WC 167 words
PD 28 April 2017
ET 02:58
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, Apr 28, BNS – Danske Bank, the second-biggest financial group in Northern Europe by assets, netted an unaudited profit of 2.5 million euros from core activities of corporate and private banking in Lithuania in the first quarter of this year, down by 25 percent, from 3.3 million euros, year-on-year.

Pretax earnings from core activities dropped by 17 percent to 2.9 million euros, according to the bank's 2016 financial report.

TD 

Total income declined by 10 percent to 4.5 million euros and operating expenses went up by 16 percent to 2.9 million euros.

Its loan portfolio increased by 3 percent over the year to 731 million euros in January-March of 2017 year-on-year, while t he deposit portfolio fell by 14 percent to 8 71 million euros.

HD  Danske Bank Q1 profit beats expectations on improved lending, strong Nordic performance
WC 236 words
PD 28 April 2017
ET 02:10
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2017 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, April 28 (Reuters) - Denmark's Danske Bank posted forecast-beating profit for the first quarter, driven by increased activity in the financial markets and higher lending.

The bank, the second-biggest in the Nordic region, is seeking to expand in Norway and Sweden where it sees significant potential for growth, despite tough competition from peers like Sweden's Nordea and Norway's DNB.

TD 

"We continued to attract new customers, especially in Norway and Sweden, and we also saw a positive trend in the volume of business with existing customers. Overall, we had a good start to the year," Chief Executive Thomas Borgen said in a statement on Friday.

The company said lending grew 4 percent from the year-earlier period, especially driven by Norway and Sweden.

Pretax profit came in at 7.14 billion Danish crowns ($1.04 billion), an increase of almost 14 percent compared with the same period last year and well above expectations for 5.98 billion in a Reuters poll.

The bank maintained its outlook for a net profit of 17-19 billion crowns this year and for long-term return on equity of 12.5 percent. The return on equity was 14.4 percent in the quarter. ($1 = 6.8474 Danish crowns) (Reporting by Stine Jacobsen and Nikolaj Skydsgaard; Editing by Subhranshu Sahu)

HD  Danske Bank earns EUR 3.4 mln profit in Q1
WC 291 words
PD 28 April 2017
ET 05:12
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Baltic News Service

LP 

TALLINN, Apr 28, BNS – Danske Bank, Estonian operation of the Danske financial group, earned a profit of 3.4 million euros in the first quarter of 2017, 9 percent more than in the same quarter a year ago.

The bank said the increase in profit was a result of loan impairment reversals arising from improved portfolio quality.

TD 

Income decreased 19 percent on a year-on-year basis. The decrease in net interest income is related to a continuing negative interest rate environment. Fee and trading income decreased as a result of somewhat lower level of customer activity and the decrease in fee income following the sale of the Estonian fund management company.

"The Estonian economy has finally recovered from a period of low economic growth. After a slowdown in recent years due to external conditions, we now expect the Estonian economy to accelerate and grow at a moderate pace over the next few years. This is reflected in business sentiment, which has become more positive lately,"Ivar Pae, head of Danske Bank Estonia, said.

The bank's net loan portfolio grew by 2 million euros, whereas deposits decreased by 404 million euros or 44 percent as the present negative interest environment means that it is better for the bank to use cross-group financing solutions instead of institutional clients from local markets.

The bank did not book additional impairment charges in the first quarter of 2017 because the quality of the loan portfolio was very good. As at March 31, accumulated impairment charges amounted to 7.8 million euros, and the ratio of impairments to loans was 0.9 percent.

Tallinn newsroom, +372 610 8823, majandus@bns.ee

Baltic News Service

HD Latvian branch of Danske Bank earns profit of EUR 0.7 million in Q1
BY LETA
WC 370 words
PD 28 April 2017
ET 06:58
SN Latvian News Agency
SC LETA
LA English
CY (c) 2017 LETA .

LP 

RIGA, April 28 (LETA) - The Latvian branch of Denmark's Danske Bank made a profit of EUR 0.7 million in the first quarter of this year, which is by 22 percent less than during the same period in 2016, the bank said. The bank's profit before impairment charges was EUR 1 million in the first quarter of 2017 or by 11 percent higher than in January-March 2016.As a result of growing business volumes, total income rose 26 percent to EUR 2.4 million in the first quarter of 2017. Net interest income grew 36 percent to EUR 1.9 million. Net fee income stood at EUR 0.5 million, unchanged year-on-year.The bank's expenses grew 30 percent compared to the first quarter of 2016, reaching EUR 1.3 million. "Because of the sale of our retail business, a larger share of expenses is now allocated to the bank's core activities.

TD 

At the same time, the bank has improved its internal processes, so we now expect lower expense growth," said Ieva Zauere, a spokeswoman for the Latvian branch of Danske Bank.The bank's deposit portfolio grew 2.1 times year-on-year to EUR 399.2 million at the end of March this year, with increases in deposits from both institutional and corporate customers. The loan portfolio for core segment customers rose 30 percent to EUR 318.6 million."Our focused approach to implementation of the strategy is paying off, and we see growing trust and cooperation with existing and new business customers. This has helped Danske Bank to show good results, although interest rates have remained low for quite a long time," said Raivis Kakanis, CEO of the Latvian branch of Danske Bank.In the first quarter of 2016, the Latvian branch of Danske Bank showed a profit of EUR 0.9 million.Danske Bank Latvia is the Latvian branch of Denmark's Danske Bank. The Latvian branch became part of the Danske Bank Group in 2007. At the end of 2016, the Latvian branch of Danske Bank was the 12th biggest bank in Latvia by assets.

HD  Danske Bank Ireland reports ‘strong performance’ in Q1
BY Colin Gleeson
WC 288 words
PD 29 April 2017
SN The Irish Times
SC IRTI
PG 16
LA English
CY (c) 2017, The Irish Times.

LP 

Danske Bank Ireland has reported a "strong performance" in the first quarter of 2017 with it on course to deliver "solid returns".

Terry Browne, country manager and head of corporate and institutional banking at Danske Bank Ireland, said: "We are pleased that our corporate and institutional division has once again delivered a strong performance, allowing us to continue to generate solid returns."

TD 

Overall, Danske Bank had a "good start" to 2017 with net profit increasing to €743.5 million from €663.7 million in the first quarter of 2016.

The result was driven by better macroeconomic developments in the Nordic countries and high customer activity at all business units.

The return on shareholders' equity after tax was 14.4 per cent, against 13.1 per cent in the first quarter of 2016.

Total income amounted to €1.7 billion, up 10 per cent from €1.5 billion in the first quarter of 2016, with increases in most income lines.

Operating expenses amounted to €769.6 million, an increase of 8 per cent from a low level in the first quarter of 2016. The increase reflected the "high activity level", and the bank's "continued focus" on digitalisation and costs related to compliance.

Loan-impairment charges remained low, with net reversals of €31.6 million in the first quarter of 2017.

In Northern Ireland, profit before tax decreased 22 per cent. The decrease was the result of reduced loan impairment reversals and increased operating expenses. The underlying performance remained "strong".

The bank said it expected to maintain its long-term outlook. "We expect net profit for 2017 to be in the range €2.2 billion- €2.6 billion," it said.

HD Education reform is key to Lithuania's economic growth - Danske Bank economist
WC 275 words
PD 18 May 2017
ET 04:56
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, May 18, BNS - Lithuania must overhaul its education system and use more high-tech solutions to maintain economic growth in the future, Danske Bank's chief economist for the Baltic countries said on Thursday.

"Lithuania now relies mostly on lower value-added production, trade and transport, but the current model will not work for long," Rokas Grajauskas said at a news conference.

TD 

"As a small nation, we must concentrate our resources and clearly identify what will drive our economy in the future and consistently work in that direction. A quality education system has to be a key element of such transformation," he said.

The economist said that a modern education system would help increase the use of high technology by companies, which would accelerate economic and wage growth.

In his opinion, for Lithuania, it would be best to focus on information and communication technology, lasers and biotechnology.

In addition to an education reform, Lithuania must also improve its tax system and labor relations and the government should be always ready to support the developing sectors of the economy, Grajauskas said.

The government has approved a higher education reform package and submitted it to the parliament for consideration. The government is also considering various secondary education changes.

Christoph Klingen, head of the International Monetary Fund's mission that concluded its work in Lithuania earlier this week, said that the country had to reform its education system -- to merge institutions and create more flexible programs -- in order to catch up with Western Europe.

Vilnius newsroom, verslas@bns.lt, +370 5 205 8511

CLM Emerging Markets Report
SE News & Commentary
HD Can investors afford to shrug off China’s credit downgrade? Danske Bank sees risk of China crisis at 50% in the long term
BY Sue Chang, MarketWatch
WC 759 words
PD 24 May 2017
ET 16:40
SN MarketWatch
SC MRKWC
LA English
CY Copyright 2017 MarketWatch, Inc. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

Danske Bank sees risk of China crisis at 50% in the long term

Moody’s Investors Service’s first downgrade of China’s sovereign rating in nearly 30 years on Wednesday has refocused attention on the country’s addiction to debt. But the subdued reaction from the global markets to the news has raised fears about complacency over mounting problems in the world’s second largest economy, according to some strategists.

TD 

“A one notch downgrade that doesn’t impact investment grade status may not be enough to spook traders any more,” said Colin Cieszynski, chief market strategist at CMC Markets.

Moody’s lowered China by one notch to A1 which is two grades above junk status. The previous ratings cut was in November 1989 in the wake of Tiananmen Square.

“The downgrade reflects Moody’s expectation that China’s financial strength will erode somewhat over the coming years, with economywide debt continuing to rise as potential growth slows,” said Moody’s in a statement.

The move puts China’s creditworthiness on par with rival Japan’s but still better than other big emerging markets such as Brazil (Ba2), Russia (Ba1), and India (Baa3). The ratings agency also lowered Hong Kong to Aa2 from Aa1, citing close links between the former British colony to China.

Global financial markets largely shrugged off the warning while the Shanghai Composite (SHCOMP, CN), which initially fell on the news, recouped its losses to edge higher at the close. The Chinese currency (USDCNY, US) also sold off but stabilized to trade at 6.89 yuan against the U.S. dollar.

“Today’s ratings downgrade reveals little that investors didn’t already know about credit growth in China and the risk that it requires the government to accept a big increase in its debt load in future,” said Mark Williams, chief China economist at Capital Economics, in a note.

Strategists also pointed out that the Chinese government has no outstanding dollar-denominated debt and most of China’s local currency debt are held by state-run banks. Foreign investors, in fact, own only about 6% of the total, according to Williams.

Nonetheless, the downgrade highlights lingering worries that the country’s reliance on credit to support its economic expansion could eventually cause problems.

“The greater concern, in our view, is not what the debt buildup is doing to government creditworthiness. Instead, it is that loose credit policies designed to prevent struggling firms from failing are eroding the economy’s long-run growth potential by preventing resources from being allocated to areas where they could be used more efficiently,” said Williams.

Not unexpectedly, Beijing criticized Moody’s downgrade as “inappropriate,” according to the official Xinhua News Agency, citing the Ministry of Finance[http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2017-05/24/c_136311925.htm?link=mktw].

“These viewpoints, to some extent, overestimate the difficulties facing the Chinese economy and underestimate the capabilities of China to deepen supply-side structural reform and expand overall demand,” the ministry said.

Chinese officials have taken steps to check the country’s voracious appetite for debt by tightening the spigot on easy money, but the consensus is that the authorities have not done enough.

China’s total debt is estimated at around 220% of gross domestic product as of 2015, with a large chunk of it owed by corporations.

There are already signs that China’s past excesses may be catching up with the economy.

The Caixin manufacturing purchasing managers index fell to a 7-month low of 50.3 in April from 51.2 in March which some blamed on tighter credit. Level 50 marks the distinction between an expansion and a contraction.

Bank of America Merrill Lynch’s China Activity Coincident Tracker, which monitors seven indicators, rose 8.5% year-over-year in April, moderating from 10.4% growth in March.

Sylvia Sheng, greater China economist at Bank of America Merrill Lynch, believes the slower reading suggests that growth momentum has peaked and will further weaken in the second half as the government continues to siphon off liquidity from the markets.

Signs of trouble in China could easily derail the world-wide equities rally and dampen global economic growth given the country’s significant role in international trade.

Meanwhile, Allan von Mehren, chief analyst at Danske Bank, played down the possibility of a financial meltdown within the next couple of years. In the longer term, however, he puts the risk of a financial crisis in China at 50%.

HD *Fitch Affirms Danske Bank AS Mortgage Cover Pool C Covered Bonds at 'AAA'
WC 2248 words
PD 26 May 2017
ET 12:28
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

26 May 2017 12:28 ET Press Release: Fitch Affirms Danske Bank AS Mortgage Cover Pool C Covered Bonds at 'AAA'

 
 
The following is a press release from Fitch Ratings:

TD 

Fitch Ratings-London-26 May 2017: Fitch Ratings has affirmed Danske Bank AS's (Danske, A/Stable/F1) mortgage covered bonds secured by the bank's cover pool C at 'AAA' with a Stable Outlook.

KEY RATING DRIVERS

- The covered bonds' rating is based on Danske's Long-Term Issuer Default Rating (IDR) of 'A' and unchanged uplifts as follows: IDR uplift of two notches; payment continuity uplift (PCU) of five notches and recovery uplift of one notch. Also, the 25.9% over-collateralisation (OC) that Fitch gives credit to and which is the lowest nominal OC of the last 12 months, provides more protection than the revised 17.0% 'AAA' breakeven OC for the programme. The latter supports a 'AA+' tested rating on a probability of default basis and a one-notch recovery uplift to 'AAA'. The Stable Outlook on the covered bonds' rating reflects that on Danske and a three-notch buffer against an issuer downgrade, due to the different uplift factors above the bank's IDR.

The reduction in Fitch 'AAA' breakeven OC for this programme, to 17.0% from 23.5%, is driven by a lower credit loss component, of 15.1% in the 'AA+' stress scenario tested for timely payment. This is mainly driven by the diminished industry correlation that Fitch now applied in its asset model to reflect that most borrowers included in the cover pool are individuals whose total income is only partially derived from the rented properties backing the loans.

In assessing the cover pool's probability of default, Fitch has assumed a three-year longer maturity for the interest-only loans (26.1%) As at 31 March 2017, Danske's cover pool C consisted of 70.8% Swedish and 29.2% Norwegian commercial real estate mortgages compared with 68.4% and 31.6%, respectively, in March 2016. Fitch calculated a 'AAA' weighted average (WA) default rate and 'AAA' WA recovery rate of 27.0% and 37.8%, respectively.

The cash flow valuation component leads to a lower 'AAA' breakeven OC by 0.6% due to positive excess spread on the underlying assets versus the covered bonds in Fitch's worst case high prepayment scenario. The asset disposal loss increases the breakeven OC by 0.8%, reflecting low maturity mismatches. The weighted average life (WAL) of the assets modelled by Fitch is 3.6 years while the WAL of the covered bonds is 2.7 years.

The programme's two-notch IDR uplift reflects that covered bonds in Denmark are exempt from bail-in, Fitch's assessment that the risk of under-collateralisation at the point of resolution is sufficiently low, and that a resolution of Danske, should it happen, would not result in the direct enforcement of the recourse against the cover pool.

Fitch's PCU for Danske's C programme is five notches, rather than the standard six for mortgage covered bonds with a 12-month principal maturity extension and three-month protection for interest payment. This is due to the lack of formal provisions to find a refinancing solution without delay in the event of a maturity extension.

The recovery uplift for this programme is capped at one notch due to the presence of significant pre-swap FX mismatches between cover assets and liabilities. The FX covered bonds are fully hedged until maturity (including the extension period). However, upon a covered bonds' default, recoveries from SEK- and NOK-denominated assets, which have a longer WAL than the covered bonds, could expose holders of non SEK- and non NOK-denominated bonds to FX risk.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

- The 'AAA' rating of Danske Bank AS's cover pool C mortgage covered bonds would be vulnerable to a downgrade if any of the following occurs: (i) Danske's Long-Term Issuer Default Rating (IDR) was downgraded by four notches to 'BBB-' or below; or (ii) the payment continuity uplift was reduced to one notch or less; or (iii) the level of overcollateralisation (OC) Fitch gives credit to in its analysis fell below the 'AAA' breakeven OC for the programme of 17.0%. If the actual OC was reduced to the legal minimum of 0%, the covered bonds would be downgraded to 'AA', three notches above the bank's IDR.

The Fitch breakeven OC for the covered bond rating will be affected, among others, by the profile of the cover assets relative to outstanding covered bonds, which can change over time, even in the absence of new issuance. Therefore the breakeven OC to maintain the covered bond rating cannot be assumed to remain stable over time.

In assessing the cover pool's probability of default, Fitch has assumed a three-year longer maturity for the interest-only loans (26.1%) As at 31 March 2017, Danske's cover pool C consisted of 70.8% Swedish and 29.2% Norwegian commercial real estate mortgages compared with 68.4% and 31.6%, respectively, in March 2016. Fitch calculated a 'AAA' weighted average (WA) default rate and 'AAA' WA recovery rate of 27.0% and 37.8%, respectively. The cash flow valuation component leads to a lower 'AAA' breakeven OC by 0.6% due to positive excess spread on the underlying assets versus the covered bonds in Fitch's worst case high prepayment scenario. The asset disposal loss increases the breakeven OC by 0.8%, reflecting low maturity mismatches. The weighted average life (WAL) of the assets modelled by Fitch is 3.6 years while the WAL of the covered bonds is 2.7 years. The programme's two-notch IDR uplift reflects that covered bonds in Denmark are exempt from bail-in, Fitch's assessment that the risk of under-collateralisation at the point of resolution is sufficiently low, and that a resolution of Danske, should it happen, would not result in the direct enforcement of the recourse against the cover pool. Fitch's PCU for Danske's C programme is five notches, rather than the standard six for mortgage covered bonds with a 12-month principal maturity extension and three-month protection for interest payment. This is due to the lack of formal provisions to find a refinancing solution without delay in the event of a maturity extension. The recovery uplift for this programme is capped at one notch due to the presence of significant pre-swap FX mismatches between cover assets and liabilities. The FX covered bonds are fully hedged until maturity (including the extension period). However, upon a covered bonds' default, recoveries from SEK- and NOK-denominated assets, which have a longer WAL than the covered bonds, could expose holders of non SEK- and non NOK-denominated bonds to FX risk. RATING SENSITIVITIES The 'AAA' rating of Danske Bank AS's cover pool C mortgage covered bonds would be vulnerable to a downgrade if any of the following occurs: (i) Danske's Long-Term Issuer Default Rating (IDR) was downgraded by four notches to 'BBB-' or below; or (ii) the payment continuity uplift was reduced to one notch or less; or (iii) the level of overcollateralisation (OC) Fitch gives credit to in its analysis fell below the 'AAA' breakeven OC for the programme of 17.0%. If the actual OC was reduced to the legal minimum of 0%, the covered bonds would be downgraded to 'AA', three notches above the bank's IDR. The Fitch breakeven OC for the covered bond rating will be affected, among others, by the profile of the cover assets relative to outstanding covered bonds, which can change over time, even in the absence of new issuance. Therefore the breakeven OC to maintain the covered bond rating cannot be assumed to remain stable over time. SE Economy
HD Quick Hits: Analysts React to U.S. Jobs Report, Look to ECB Meeting; The Atlanta Fed's GDP tracker now estimates growth in the second quarter at 3.4%, down from 4%
BY By WSJ Staff
WC 1592 words
PD 2 June 2017
ET 14:54
SN WSJ Pro Central Banking
SC RSTPROCB
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

The latest reading from the Atlanta Fed's gross domestic product growth tracker took a hit, analysts reacted to the U.S. jobs report, and the European Central Bank policy meeting and U.K. general election will make next week a big one for Europe. Here are quick hits on central banking and related market views from around the world.

Atlanta Fed Takes Big Bite Out of 2nd-Quarter GDP Estimate

TD 

The latest iteration of the Atlanta Fed's GDPNow real-time growth tracker just took a hit, moving from a potential sizzler to something merely hot. The bank says it now estimates growth in the second quarter at 3.4%, down notably from the 4% prediction Thursday. The jobs data's to blame: The bank says it is now estimating a slower gain in consumer spending.

Michael S. Derby

Jobs Report Shouldn't Derail the Fed, Strategist Says

The jobs report showed the pace of hiring slowed in May, with nonfarm payrolls rising by 138,000, below the 184,000 expected by economists surveyed by WSJ. But that shouldn't translate to a weak labor market or economy, according to Sean Lynch, co-head of global equity strategy at Wells Fargo Investment Institute. "I think the number had to be a pretty big outlier to the downside to really knock the Fed off the course, and we didn't get that," said Mr. Lynch. "I think we are growing but probably growing modestly. That's probably the recipe for low volatility in the market."

Liying Qian

Weaker-Than-Expected May Payrolls Could Give Fed Caution

The May jobs report could lead the Fed to take a more cautious attitude, said Russell Price, senior economist at Ameriprise Financial. The Fed is still likely to raise overnight lending rates 25 basis points at its June 13-14 meeting, he said, but officials might look for signs of a pickup in activity before committing to another increase beyond that meeting. Still, Price expects the Fed to raise rates a total of three times in 2017. "Consumer and corporate borrowing costs may not necessarily rise in lock step," he added, "but we believe the economy is strong enough to absorb the increases if they do."

Daisy Maxey

Brexit Talks May Hurt Economy, but BOE Won't Budge

Risks to the U.K. economy next year are "tilted to the downside," depending on how negotiations between the British government and the European Union go, Moody's said in a note. The Brexit negotiations and anxiety regarding the U.K's future should dampen sentiment. But the Bank of England is unlikely to tighten monetary policy, even in the face of inflationary pressures. Moody's expects the BOE to postpone tightening until "well after" the U.K. exits from the EU, with the first interest-rate rise coming in mid-2019.

Tasos Vossos

June 8 Poised to Be Action Day

Two major events will grab investors' attention, and possibly drag their nerves, on June 8 when the U.K. holds a general election and the European Central Bank possibly takes its first tentative step toward policy normalization. As for the ECB's meeting, focus will be on potential changes to the forward guidance in a less "dovish" direction, Danske Bank said. Danske, however, doesn't expect the ECB to make any changes, to avoid any risk of an unwarranted tightening. In the U.K, the most recent polls continue to point to a win for Prime Minister Theresa May even if the gap between Labour and the Conservatives has narrowed of late.

Emese Bartha

ECB Exit to be Painfully Slow, Commerzbank Says

The European Central Bank's ending of its very aggressive monetary policy will be the opposite of ripping off a Band-Aid, Commerzbank said in a note Friday. It said the ECB won't end its bond purchase program until the end of next year, and this will be more for legal reasons that could arise if it owned more than one-third of government bonds. "In other words, the end of bond purchases will be a measure forced on the Bank. Investors should not confuse the end of these purchases with a general end to a lax monetary stance," Commerzbank said. Steadily low core inflation will give the ECB grounds to keep rates unchanged until well beyond the end of bond purchases. "The retreat from its current monetary position will no doubt be a painfully slow process."

Todd Buell

ECB to De-Emphasize Further Rate Cut

The ECB next Thursday will play down the possibility of a further rate cut, Berenberg said in a note Friday. "The ECB could do so by committing to keeping rates at ‘present' instead of ‘present or lower' levels for ‘an extended period of time'," said Berenberg, adding that the ECB wouldn't "rule out" a further rate cut. It could still rhetorically keep the door open for a cut by saying that should economic conditions worsen it could "relax its monetary stance further." Berenberg says this "would include the option of a potential rate cut but in a more low-key way than before."

Todd Buell

Draghi Seen Pointing to Low Core Inflation

European Central Bank President Mario Draghi likely will highlight a solid economic recovery in the eurozone at his press conference next week, while citing low core inflation as a reason not to make any major changes, said Franck Dixmier, global head of fixed income and chief investment officer for fixed income at Allianz Global Investors. Mr. Dixmier expects the ECB will convey the message that eurozone states are making synchronized progress on the road to recovery and that the downside risk potential has significantly decreased. The ECB probably will seek to justify keeping its antideflationary measures in place, pointing to stubbornly low core inflation.

Emese Bartha

ECB Hints on QE Tapering to Come During Q&A

Investors looking for hints on the future of the European Central Bank's quantitative-easing program at next week's meeting shouldn't be disappointed if the statement's language is unchanged. Instead, they should wait until the Q&A, when President Mario Draghi likely will say the governing council is starting to discuss the exit strategy, Berenberg economist Holger Schmieding said. But Mr. Draghi won't commit the ECB to a particular course of action yet.

Tasos Vossos

ECB QE Has Expiration Date, and Portugal is Due First

Even if the European Central Bank surprises everyone in the market and decides to continue quantitative easing at the current pace of €60 billion ($67.4 billion) a month, the program still has an "expiration date," according to Société Générale. The French bank defines this as the time the ECB hits either the issuer or issue limit on a country's sovereign debt. And the first one to reach its expiration date will be Portugal, in April 2018, followed by Finland and Germany later next year. The last one to "expire" will be Belgium in June 2021, based on Société Générale calculations.

Tasos Vossos

ECB Credit QE Success Doubtful

The European Central Bank's corporate bond purchase scheme is expected to end at some point next year, but whether the ECB can feel pleased with the credit quantitative easing's results remains unclear, Commerzbank said. Granted, funding costs for corporates in the euro bond market declined. But companies used this as an opportunity to refinance debt at lower interest rates and optimize their funding instead of financing investment projects. Meanwhile, investors are left with the negative side effects or even patchier secondary market liquidity and increasing spread correlations between frequent and infrequent issuers, which reduce the benefit of portfolio diversification, the German bank says. Analysts expect the ECB to announce tapering later this year, with actual implementation coming in 2018.

Tasos Vossos

Citi Sees 1st South Korea Rate Hike Coming in 1Q

South Korea's economy will grow at "a little steeper" pace than expected this year, likely prompting the central bank to start raising interest rates in 2018, Citi posited. The investment bank raises its 2017 gross domestic product growth view to 2.9% from 2.6%, given the first quarter's strength, the new government's planned extra budget and solid exports. The Bank of Korea's revised growth data show GDP rose 1.1% from the fourth quarter last quarter, the most in six quarters. Citi sees the first rate increase coming in the first quarter of 2018, followed by another in the second half of the year.

Kwanwoo Jun

RBA Set to Look Through Weather Wobbles

Cyclone Debbie and a very wet March on the east coast are likely to have weakened first-half Australian gross domestic product growth, said HSBC. But it thinks that for the country's central bank, weather-related GDP wobbles will make little difference to policy, as other measures like surveyed business conditions and employment indicators—which are better at discounting such a weather impact—have held up well in recent months. HSBC expects the RBA to be firmly on hold and reiterate it expects growth to lift the next couple of years and underlying inflation to gradually climb.

James Glynn

(The items in this column come from Market Talk, a feature of Dow Jones Newswires [https://www.dowjones.com/products/newswires/] that provides real-time analysis of news developments and market activity.)

SE Economy
HD Quick Hits: Views on This Week's ECB Meeting; Political turmoil is making Brazil's central bank reluctant in its forecasts
BY By WSJ Staff
WC 824 words
PD 6 June 2017
ET 14:37
SN WSJ Pro Central Banking
SC RSTPROCB
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

Analysts give their views on what to expect from this week's European Central Bank meeting, the political situation in Brazil has complicated the central bank's outlook, and HSBC analysts examine how the People's Bank of China can pursue both a stable and flexible exchange rate. Here are quick hits on central banking and related market views from around the world.

Danske Expects ECB to Stick to Forward Guidance

TD 

Danske believes it is too early for the European Central Bank to change its forward guidance at its meeting Thursday. "In our view, it [the ECB] will take a more cautious approach in order to avoid an unwarranted tightening of the financial conditions, which would reduce the likelihood of the underlying price pressure building up," Danske said. Instead of changing forward guidance, the ECB may change its rhetoric regarding the growth outlook, saying that risks to growth are largely balanced instead of "to the downside." This should eventually lead to a change to the forward guidance, but Danske thinks this step is too risky for the ECB for now.

Emese Bartha

ECB Likely to Tweak Language but Only Modestly

Oxford Economics sees only modest tweaks to the European Central Bank's introductory statement Thursday and in the language used by President Mario Draghi at his press conference. While eurozone activity data released since the ECB's March staff forecasts have been "unambiguously positive," this is unlikely to translate into a higher inflation forecast, said Ben May, Oxford Economics' lead eurozone economist. Indeed, eurozone headline inflation may actually be revised lower for this year due to recent oil price weakness and the stronger euro, and there is little evidence of a pickup in underlying inflation pressures, he added.

Emese Bartha

ECB to Detail Plans for Bond Buying in September, Says ING

ING doesn't see the European Central Bank saying much about tapering bond purchases on Thursday, but it does see President Mario Draghi possibly mentioning a further reduction in quantitative easing in September, when the ECB usually announces what it plans to do in the first quarter of the following year. In the next three months, the ECB "will change in how it views the world," said Chris Turner, global head of strategy at ING. "Why do you need bond buying if the economy is growing?" he asked, pointing to the fact that the eurozone "economic recovery is widespread" and driven by domestic demand, not just exports.

Olga Cotaga

ECB Can Avoid ‘Taper Tantrum' With Sticky Easing Bias

One way for the European Central Bank to avoid a "taper tantrum," similar to what the Federal Reserve had to deal with in 2013, is to reduce asset purchases while keeping its easing bias, TD Securities said. This means the ECB could taper alongside a message that there is nothing that could hasten the pace of quantitative-easing reduction and that the program could still be boosted if necessary. Still, the Canadian bank acknowledged such a tapering/easing bias combination seems "a bit odd."

Tasos Vossos

Politics Jumble Brazil's Central Bank Outlook

Political turmoil is making Brazil's central bank reluctant in its forecasts. The bank said in minutes to last week's meeting, when it cuts its benchmark Selic rate to 10.25% from 11.25%, that next month the trimming could be smaller, while pointing out that the "balance of risks" requires close monitoring. The bank said there still is a lot of slack in the economy and prices are weak, but fiscal reform needed to ensure long-term stability is now less certain thanks to political gridlock. The bank said some members argued for not making any guidance at all this time, but the prevailing argument was that there was "a need, at this point, to offer…elements to reduce uncertainty about monetary policy."

Paulo Trevisani

What Does China Mean by a Stable and Flexible Exchange Rate?

China's central bank has long said it aims for a stable exchange rate and a flexible exchange rate, according to HSBC analysts, who then ask the next logical question: How can you have both at once? The answer lies in the People's Bank of China's murky definition of stability. The HSBC analysts interpret that definition as basically steady relative to other major currencies and relative to its fair value, which keeps changing. And since the fair value keeps changing, that means the exchange rate will have to be flexible enough to end up near that new level. The emphasis on flexibility—gains and declines in the yuan—is also an attempt to change investors' expectations about the path of the Chinese currency.

Saumya Vaishampayan

(The items in this column come from Market Talk, a feature of Dow Jones Newswires [https://www.dowjones.com/products/newswires/] that provides real-time analysis of news developments and market activity.)

EXEL COMPOSITES PLC          STOCK EXCHANGE RELEASE          7 JUNE 2017 
at 12:30 EET 
Exel Composites Plc has on 7 June 2017 received a disclosure under 
Chapter 9, Section 5 of the Finnish Securities Markets Act according to 
which the holding of Danske Bank A/S has exceeded 5% of the voting 
rights and share capital in Exel Composites Plc. 
 
Through share transactions concluded on 6 June 2017, the total holding 
of Danske Bank A/S amounts to 603,658 shares representing 5.07% of the 
shares and voting rights of the Company. 
 
Exel Composites has a total of 11,896,843 shares. There is only one 
class of shares, each share entitling one vote. 
 
Vantaa, 7 June 2017 
 
Exel Composites Plc 
 
Mikko Kettunen 
CFO

Exel Composites in brief 
 
Exel Composites (www.exelcomposites.com[http://www.exelcomposites.com]) is a leading composite 
technology company that designs, manufactures and markets composite 
products and solutions for demanding applications. Exel Composites 
provides superior customer experience through continuous innovation, 
world-class operations and long-term partnerships. 
 
The core of the operations is based on own, internally developed 
composite technology, product range based on it and strong market 
position in selected segments with a strong quality and brand image. 
Profitable growth is pursued by a relentless search for new applications 
and development in co-operation with customers. The personnels 
expertise and high level of technology play a major role in Exel 
Composites operations. Exel Composites Plc share is listed in Nasdaq 
Helsinki Ltd.

HD Fitch Updates Bespoke Swedish Residential Mortgage Criteria; No Rating Impact
WC 1429 words
PD 9 June 2017
ET 11:22
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2017 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

(The following statement was released by the rating agency) Link to Fitch Ratings' Report: Swedish Mortgage Danske Bank Bespoke Rating Criteria https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/899150[https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/899150] LONDON, June 09 (Fitch) Fitch Ratings has updated its bespoke rating criteria for Swedish residential mortgages originated by Danske Bank. The criteria assumptions are used for analysing Swedish residential mortgages when rating Danske Bank's Cover Pool I covered bond programme. The update does not have any rating impact on the existing covered bonds rated by the agency. The updated criteria only include minor changes and some simplifications. Notably, Fitch has removed the frequency of foreclosure hits for loans with payment frequency other than monthly. The foreclosure frequency assumptions for Swedish residential mortgage loans are otherwise unchanged, reflecting the low observed default rate for such assets.

TD 

This is underpinned by the high social security benefits in Sweden that provide a safety net in case of unemployment, and the robust economic growth during the past few years. The updated criteria also detail the treatment of loan margins in Fitch's cash-flows modelling. The agency applies a haircut below the lowest observed margin of the last 12 months. Fitch's house price decline assumptions remain high at 54% and 48% in a 'AAA' scenario for Stockholm and the rest of the country, and at 15% in a 'B' scenario. This reflects Fitch's view that house prices are above their sustainable level, having increased at a faster pace than household income for a prolonged period. The full criteria report is available on www.fitchratings.com[http://www.fitchratings.com] or by clicking the link above. HD Danske Bank Markets predicts Norway rate hike in summer 2018
WC 344 words
PD 15 June 2017
ET 03:00
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2017 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

TD 

     * Lifts Norway mainland growth to 2.0 pct in 2017, 2.3 pct
in 2018
    * Sees activity level recovering to normal level in 2019
    * Predicts central bank will remove easing bias next week
    * Does not expect crash in housing market
    * Expects stronger NOK in the longer run

    OSLO, June 15 (Reuters) - Growth in Norway's economy has
been stronger than expected and will necessitate a central bank
rate hike in the summer of 2018, Danske Bank Markets said on
Thursday.
    Economists at the brokerage raised forecasts for growth in
Norway's mainland economy to 2.0 percent for 2017 and 2.3
percent in 2018 from previously 1.8 and 2.2 percent
respectively.
    "It is now time to start discussing the timing of the first
rate hike in Norway, which we think will come in the third
quarter next year," Danske's Chief Economist Frank Jullum told
Reuters.
    It would be the first time since 2011 that the central bank
raises the cost of borrowing.
    Jullum predicted the central bank will meanwhile remove its
so-called easing bias next week, eliminating the risk of further
rate cuts.
    In March Norges Bank said the key policy rate would most
likely remain close to the current level of 0.5 percent for the
next few years, but added there was a slightly higher
probability of a cut than a hike in the year ahead. 
    Falling unemployment and continued low interest rates will
likely prevent a crash in housing prices, Danske said.
    The Norwegian crown is expected to strengthen in the
"slightly longer run", supported by higher oil prices and
stronger growth, the brokerage added.

    Norway economy forecasts by Danske Bank (numbers in percent,
estimates from March in brackets):

                                   2017          2018           
 
 MAINLAND GDP                   2.0  (1.8)    2.3  (2.2)        
 PRIVATE CONSUMPTION            2.0  (2.1)    2.3  (2.3)        
 UNEMPLOYMENT (NAV)             2.7  (2.8)    2.6  (2.7)

 (Reporting by Camilla Knudsen, editing by Terje Solsvik)

HD  Sampo Oyj The Valuation Of Mandatum Life's Portfolio To Be Sold To Danske Bank Finalized
WC 484 words
PD 19 June 2017
ET 09:45
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

 
TIDMSAMPO 
 
 
   SAMPO PLC            STOCK EXCHANGE RELEASE         19 June 2017 at 4:45 
pm 
 
   The valuation of Mandatum Life's portfolio to be sold to Danske Bank 
finalized 
 
   Mandatum Life Insurance Co. Ltd. disclosed on 27 October 2016 that it 
will exercise its option to sell the insurance portfolio, sold through 
Danske Bank's branch network in Finland, to Danske Bank or its nominee. 
The valuation process, by which the value of the portfolio was to be 
determined, is now finalized by the external valuators. 
 
   As a result of the valuation process the value of the insurance 
portfolio as at the 31 December 2016 is EUR 334 million. Mandatum Life 
and Danske Bank have agreed that the theoretical result from the 
beginning of 2017 until the date of the transfer as determined in the 
valuation process will be deducted from the final sales price. This 
theoretical result for year 2017 is determined to be EUR 18.1 million 
and for year 2018 EUR 18.6 million. Mandatum Life and Danske Bank have 
agreed that the actual result produced by the portfolio until the 
transfer remains with Mandatum Life. The Transitional Agency Agreement 
between Mandatum Life and Danske Bank will continue until closing. 
 
   After the transfer has been completed the transaction is expected to 
have a negative impact of EUR 20 - 25 million on Mandatum Life's annual 
profit before taxes. The transfer of the portfolio is expected to take 
place during 2018. 
 
   For Mandatum Life sales gain from the transaction equals the value of 
the insurance portfolio adjusted with items explained in the previous 
chapter. The sales gain is taxable under the Finnish tax law. In Sampo 
Group's consolidated accounts a goodwill of approximately EUR 75 million 
will be deducted from the sales gain. The transaction will have a 
positive impact on Mandatum Life's solvency position. 
 
   The sale of the portfolio is related to Mandatum Life's decision of not 
prolonging its agency agreement with Danske Bank as of 31 December 2016. 
In relation to the agency agreement Mandatum Life had the right to sell 
the insurance portfolio, sold through Danske Bank's branch network in 
Finland, to Danske Bank.

SE TRADING POST
HD Trading Post
BY By Michael Hunter
WC 254 words
PD 20 June 2017
SN Financial Times
SC FTFTA
ED USA Ed1
PG 19
LA English
CY Copyright 2017 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web.

LP 

Midsummer in Scandinavia is famed for long, unbroken daylight and a sense of revelry.

The full extent of the festive mood is not expected to reach Thursday's meeting of the Norway's central bank, which is set to turn only "cautiously hawkish", according to Danske Bank.

TD 

While that approach means policy will be left on hold, Danske also thinks the Norges Bank will "remove the cut probability embedded into the rate path entirely", leaving it on course to lift rates next time there is a change.

"We pencil in the first rate hike around end-2018," says Kristoffer Kjær Lomholt, senior analyst.

Amid the midsummer change in outlook, the Norwegian krone "seems fundamentally undervalued" at NKr9.44 to the euro, with Danske citing NKr8.43 as "a long term fair-value anchor".

But that is not just because of improving data out of Norway, although labour market and Regional Network survey data are on the up.

Danske added: "While we don't expect the Norges Bank, global growth or commodity markets to add much support to the krone near-term, broad-based euro weakness could trigger an implicit 'krone-revival' in the coming months.

"The Norwegian normalisation story, valuation and real rates remain clear krone positives, but the effects will likely be [more apparent in the] second half of 2017/first half of 2018."

So, expect the Norges Bank's midsummer meeting to be felt most once the seasons have changed.

michael.hunter@ft.com

HD Lithuanian Business Leader Awards handed out for 7th time

LP 

Vilnius, June 22 (ELTA) - The Lithuanian Business Leader Award ceremony, organised by daily business newspaper Verslo Zinios and bank Nordea, took place for the seventh time. Awards were presented to successful companies and the CEO of the Year.

UAB Kitron received the Exporter of the Year award. Other nominees in the category included UAB Espersen Lietuva and UAB Scapa Baltic.

TD 

The Employer of the Year award went to Danske Bank A/S Lithuania branch. Companies that were nominated included UAB Lidl Lietuva and UAB PKC Group Lithuania

UAB Interlux, providing technologies and solutions for medicine, science and biotechnology industries, received the Responsible Business award. UAB Freda and UAB Mars Lietuva were nominated in the category.

Real estate project development company UAB BaltischesHaus won in the Business of the Year category. Other nominees included UAB Fortum Klaipeda and UAB Novikontas SCM.

Readers o vz.lt named Petras Masiulis, the head of telecommunications company UAB Tele2, as the CEO of the Year.

Darius Eidukonis, the head of freight forwarding company UAB MDI Transport, was named the Young CEO of the Year. Others nominees were Erikas Butnoris from agricultural cooperative Vidukle and Mindaugas Apanavicius from UAB Sominis Technology.

Company announcement    Danske Bank Plc 
                         26 June 2017 
 
 
   Board of Directors of Danske Bank Plc approves merger plan 
 
   As announced on 2 February 2017, Danske Bank A/S is looking into the 
possibilities of merging its activities in Finland into a single Finnish 
branch. As a part of this process, the Board of Directors of Danske Bank 
Plc has on 26 June 2017 approved a plan aiming at merging Danske Bank 
Plc with its parent company Danske Bank A/S. The merger is expected to 
take effect from 31 December 2017. 
 
   The merger is subject to the final approval by the Board of Directors of 
Danske Bank Plc and relevant approvals from the authorities. 
 
   Following the merger, our bank services will be offered in Finland by 
Danske Bank A/S Finland branch. Through the planned merger, the Danske 
Bank Group will achieve a uniform, simple organisational structure 
across the Nordic markets. The simpler our organization is, the easier 
it is for us to develop our services to the benefit of our customers. 
 
   The planned merger will be primarily of a technical nature and will not 
change the way in which we serve our customers, nor will employees 
experience changes.

SE Economy
HD Quick Hits: Review Recommends Monetary Policy Committee at Norges Bank; San Francisco Fed's Williams warns of a ‘hot economy' if rate increases slow
BY By WSJ Staff
WC 996 words
PD 26 June 2017
ET 14:21
SN WSJ Pro Central Banking
SC RSTPROCB
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

A review of Norway's central bank suggested the bank have a separate monetary policy board, San Francisco Fed chief John Williams warned of a "hot economy" if interest rates aren't raised farther, and mortgage tightening in China may widen. Here are quick hits on central banking and related market views from around the world.

Review Recommends Monetary Policy Committee at Norges Bank

TD 

Friday's Norges Bank review didn't include any new regulation regarding Norwegian monetary policy, but did suggest that the Government Pension Fund Global, or oil fund, be organized outside of the central bank, and that Norges Bank should have a separate monetary policy board, noted Danske Bank. "In essence, this illustrates that Norway is taking more and more steps towards making monetary policy actions independent of oil in preparing the economy for the future." The Norwegian government appointed a committee in 2015, chaired by former central bank Gov. Svein Gjedrem, to review the Central Bank Act and the governance of Norges Bank. Its proposals suggest that the central bank's mandate will remain that of flexible inflation targeting, albeit the target could be lowered, as many market participants have been anticipating, Danske added.

Dominic Chopping

Fed's Williams Fears ‘Hot Economy' if Rate Increases Slow

San Francisco Fed chief John Williams fears a "hot economy" if interest rates aren't raised farther, but similarly he doesn't want to see the U.S. economy stall. That as he said in Sydney that current policy trends are consistent with above-trend gross domestic product. "The path we are on has worked OK in the sense that if we raise rates three times this year and three or four times next year, it is consistent with what you see in our projections. That's consistent with an economy growing at or above trend, inflation moving back to 2% and getting that balance of not too hot, not too cold."

James Glynn

Chinese Mortgage Tightening May Widen

Smaller Chinese cities have been seeing faster home-price increases of late, which may be a good thing and could help clear a glut of available properties in such locales. But authorities are worried those markets will become just as bubbly as in the biggest cities. China's chief banking regulator, Guo Shuqing, recently said regional housing bubbles need to be contained—ideally by controlling the pace of mortgage lending through higher rates and shorter repayment periods. "We expect that the [China Banking Regulatory Commission] or the [People's Bank of China] will become more involved with mortgage policy for such cities," said SHKF Research.

Dominique Fong

BOC Official to Go Off Record as Rate Decision Nears

A senior Bank of Canada official, deputy governor Lawrence Schembri, was to speak at a Toronto event for business economists in an off-the-record session. According to organizers, Mr. Schembri was to discuss "Four Puzzles Within an Outlook" at an event closed to the media. It isn't on the official BOC events calendar. Bank of Nova Scotia economist Derek Holt said there is "always the risk of street chatter" emerging from such an event. The appearance comes just over two weeks before the BOC delivers its next rate policy decision, which has taken on heightened interest given the central bank's sudden "hawkish" tilt. Mr. Holt added that such events "create the optics of not communicating publicly everything that BOC may be saying privately." BOC Gov. Stephen Poloz and deputy governor Lynn Patterson both have public speaking engagements Wednesday.

Paul Vieira

Sterling Rates Turn Most ‘Hawkish' Since Early 2016

Derivatives tied to the Sterling Overnight Index Average, or Sonia, point to a 100% probability of a rate increase in the coming 12-18 months for the first time since the start of 2016, Société Générale said in a note. And Bank of England chief economist Andy Haldane's recent comments that he expects to vote for a rate increase later in 2017 "have precipitated this re-pricing," the French bank added. The BOE's policy rate still stands at a record-low of 0.25%. The central bank has already completed gilt and corporate bond purchases announced last August in the wake of the vote to leave the European Union.

Tasos Vossos

Morgan Stanley Advises Buying GBP/JPY, Target 152

Buy GBP/JPY at the market price, says Morgan Stanley, which forecasts a rise to 152. It advises to stop buying if GBP/JPY reaches 139. The recommendation is largely based on expectations of falls in the yen due to growing appetite for risk, while Morgan Stanley also noted that Japanese investors have been buying foreign assets without a foreign-exchange hedge. It sees the British pound as a better bet to buy against the yen rather than the dollar, with the pound seen supported by increased prospects of a U.K. rate rise and "emerging signs of political stability." "Markets may assign higher probabilities to the [Bank of England] hiking rates this year, providing GBP strength," Morgan Stanley said.

Olga Cotaga

Signs Covered Bond Market Positions Against ECB Tapering

Solid demand for last week's euro covered bonds that aren't eligible for European Central Bank purchases could reflect investors' expectations that the ECB will reduce its presence in the market, ABN Amro strategists say. The so-called quantitative-easing tapering will have a more limited impact on bonds that haven't benefited directly from ECB purchases. Analysts generally expect the ECB to announce tapering in September and implement it in 2018. For now, the central bank is scheduled to buy €60 billion ($67 billion) of assets, including covered bonds, each month until at least December.

Tasos Vossos

HD  Danske Bank eyes €2bn sale of retail loan book
BY Gretchen Friemann
WC 379 words
PD 29 June 2017
SN Irish Independent
SC IINM
ED 1; National
PG 1
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Independent Newspapers Ireland Ltd

LP 

DANSKE Bank is mulling a sale of more than €2bn of performing Irish home loans and buyto-let mortgages as the Danish lender continues to manage down its retail business here to focus solely on corporate and institutional clients.

The bank is understood to be considering a portfolio sale or potentially rolling the loans into a securitisation deal.

TD 

It is understood Morgan Stanley is advising Danske, with a deal likely to be concluded by the end of the year.

The bank declined to comment, however sources said a number of prospective suitors have already cast an eye over the portfolio including private equity firms and Irish banks struggling to grow their loan books because of housing shortages.

Bank of Ireland is widely viewed as a logical suitor after earlier snapping up €274m of performing commercial loans from Danske in 2015.

The deal was part of a wider €540m disposal that resulted in Goldman Sachs hoovering up €266m of toxic debt bundled into the sale.

It is understood Danske has long targeted an exit and had hoped to agree a sale by the autumn.

The Danish bank, which entered the local market with the acquisition of National Irish Bank, pulled down the shutters on its personal and business lending operations in October 2013 after nursing substantial losses.

Loans linked to its former retail bank were moved into a work-out unit while the day-today management of its personal mortgages book, which stood at DKK17.4bn (€2.3bn) in 2015, was outsourced to Pepper Asset Services.

Sources said the home loans portfolio include some buyto-let loans as well as primary residential mortgages.

It's also thought to include a significant volume of tracker mortgages, which could weigh on the final sale price given the loans' low profitability.

While Danske is considering offloading the portfolio in one tranche, sources said a securitisation may also be on the cards.

However packaging the loans into bonds would be expensive and management intensive.

Earlier this year Mars Capital, a big buyer of Irish mortgages securitised €332m worth of sub-prime loans.

The firm, which is linked to Oaktree Capital bundled together the mortgages into a special purpose vehicle called, Grand Canal Securities 1.

HD *S&PGR Affirms Danske Bank At 'A/A-1'; Outlook Stable
WC 2127 words
PD 30 June 2017
ET 11:28
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

30 Jun 2017 11:28 ET Press Release: S&PGR Affirms Danske Bank At 'A/A-1'; Outlook Stable

TD 

 
 
The following is a press release from Standard & Poor's: 
 
     -- Danske Bank has achieved its internal return on equity targets ahead 
of schedule, and appears well positioned to continue keeping pace with 
Europe's top performing banks. 
     -- The bank's strong performance is contributing significant value and 
payouts to shareholders, while maintaining risk-adjusted capital ratios at 
10.25%-10.75%. 
     -- We are therefore affirming our 'A/A-1' ratings on Danske Bank and its 
core operating subsidiary Danske Bank PLC, as well as our 'A' rating on core 
insurance subsidiary Danica Pension Livsforsikringsaktieselskab. 
     -- The stable outlook reflects our expectation of steady capital levels 
and a slow buildup of additional loss-absorbing capacity buffers. 
 
STOCKHOLM (S&P Global Ratings) June 30, 2017--S&P Global Ratings said today it 
has affirmed its 'A/A-1' long- and short-term counterparty credit ratings on 
Denmark-based Danske Bank A/S and core subsidiary Danske Bank PLC, as well as 
its 'A' long-term counterparty credit rating on Danica Pension 
Livsforsikringsaktieselskab (Danica). The outlooks on these entities remain 
stable. 
 
We also affirmed our issue credit ratings on these entities' subordinated and 
hybrid capital instruments. 
 
The affirmation reflects our view that Danske Bank's strong earnings 
performance will continue to translate into high payouts for shareholders, 
with risk-adjusted capital (RAC) ratios staying slightly above the 10.2% 
achieved at year-end 2016. Danske Bank has exceeded our expectations by 
achieving its 2018 goal of a 12.5% return on equity (ROE) in 2016, with an ROE 
of 13.2%. Due to a few positive one-time items last year, we anticipate 
somewhat lower returns in 2017, but believe the bank will maintain or exceed 
these return targets this year and in 2018, placing it firmly among Europe's 
top-tier banks in terms of profits and efficiency. 
 
Danske Bank continues to focus on optimizing its capital structure, including 
a $750 million additional tier 1 capital instrument issued in March 2017. 
These efforts are reflected in the significant share buyback programs of 
Danish krone (DKK) 9 billion (about EUR1.2 billion) in 2016 and a DKK10 billion 
program initiated in 2017, complementing the 45% annual dividend payout, 
resulting in average expected payout ratios of over 90% in 2016 and 2017. 
Beyond that, we expect the bank will retain a somewhat higher share of 
earnings in order to expand in the Nordic markets and maintain its regulatory 
common equity tier 1 target range of 14%-15%. 
 
We continue to hold the view that Danske Bank's key position in the Danish 
banking market and complementary Nordic businesses are rating strengths. 
Danske Bank is the second-largest bank in the Nordics and in addition to a 
25%-30% market share in Denmark, is one of two banks with material personal, 
corporate, and capital markets businesses in each of those markets, improving 
risk and revenue diversification. Recoveries from legacy nonperforming loans 
(NPLs) have contributed positively to net profits in eight of the last nine 
quarters, and we anticipated NPLs will remain below five basis points of total 
lending in the coming years. 
 
Danske Bank has a leading position as a deposit-taker in Denmark and a 
significant role in the well-functioning Danish mortgage market. Although 
Danske Bank uses a higher share of covered bond financing than many of its 
international peers (36% of the funding base), we see the stability and unique 
features of the Danish covered bond market as neutral to the bank's funding 
profile. 
 
We do not include any uplift for additional loss-absorbing capacity (ALAC) in 
our long-term rating on Danske Bank. We anticipate that the Danish regulator 
will eventually require a large share of bail-in-able liabilities as it 
outlines its minimum requirements for banks' own funds and eligible 
liabilities. But we will await further clarity before anticipating an increase 
of such instruments at the bank. 
 
The stable outlook on Danske Bank and its core subsidiaries reflects our view 
that the bank will maintain its strong capital and improved profitability, 
even as it pays out a significant share of annual profits via dividends and 
share buyback programs. In our view, Danske Bank maintains some capital 
flexibility in addition to our RAC ratio metric, which is likely to stay 
within the 10.25%-10.75% range. We believe that the prospect of higher 
regulatory capital requirements and flexibility to discontinue high payout 
levels support this view. Nevertheless, we note that negative trends in the 
banking sector in Danske Bank's key markets--Norway, Sweden, and the 
U.K.--could affect our view of the bank's capital ratios. We also expect 
Danske Bank will maintain its stock of instruments, which we consider eligible 
for ALAC buffers, below 4.5% of our risk-weighted assets (RWA) measure over 
the coming two years. 
 
A negative rating action on Danske Bank is currently unlikely, given 
improvements in the bank's performance and strengthening of Denmark's economy. 
Furthermore, we note the bank would still have meaningful ALAC buffers, even 
if its stand-alone capital and earnings declined to adequate from strong. 
 
We could take a positive rating action if the buildup of Danske Bank's ALAC 
exceeded our expectations, with the buffer reaching at least 4.5% of our RWA 
figure on a sustainable basis. 
 
The stable outlook on subsidiary Danica reflects that on Danske Bank, since we 
view Danica as a core group entity, and our alignment of the rating with the 
unsupported group credit profile.
