SE Pro Private Markets
HD Investment Chiefs at Danske Private Equity Step Down
BY By Ed Ballard
WC 257 words
PD 30 June 2017
ET 08:02
SN WSJ Pro Private Equity
SC RSTPROPE
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

The two investment chiefs leading Danske Bank A/S's private-equity arm have stepped down following an internal reorganization of its asset management and private-equity platforms.

Managing Partner John Danielsen and Senior Partner Peter Thellufsen have left the fund-of-funds investor after the Danish bank "decided to integrate Danske Private Equity more closely into Danske Bank Asset Management," according to a statement.

TD 

Mr. Danielsen and Mr. Thellufsen led a nine-strong investment team based in Copenhagen, according to the firm's website. Danske Private Equity invests in small and midmarket buyout funds in Europe and the U.S. and manages investor commitments of €3.7 billion ($4.22 billion), the statement said.

The division will now be overseen by newly appointed Chief Executive Michael Nørgaard, a member of Danske Private Equity's board who was previously a senior vice president in Danske Bank's Treasury.

Mr. Nørgaard "has extensive experience with private equity, managing the bank's private equity and unlisted securities portfolios," the statement said.

The objective of the reshuffle "is to strengthen Danske's combined investment competences within private equity and alternative investments in general," Danske said.

The bank added: "Private equity will remain a separate legal entity, with AIFM authorisation [under the EU's Alternative Investment Fund Managers Directive] and will continue to pursue the same strategy and ambitions. However, the combination will lead to operational synergies."

Write to Ed Ballard at ed.ballard@wsj.com [mailto:ed.ballard@wsj.com]

HD Davy Private buys £500m wealth business from Danske
BY Yoosof Farah
WC 269 words
PD 10 July 2017
SN Citywire
SC CWIRE
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Citywire.co.uk. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

Davy Private Clients has acquired Danske Bank's discretionary portfolio management wealth business for an undisclosed sum.

The deal involves the transfer of over 1,100 Danske Bank customer investment portfolios, currently managed by the bank's investment centre, which are scheduled to move across to Davy by the end of October this year.

TD 

Davy said there will be no redundancies associated with the acquisition, with twelve Danske Bank employees expected to join Davy as part of the deal.

The agreement also sees Danske Bank make Davy its preferred referral partner for private banking customers seeking options to invest over £150,000.

Richard Caldwell, managing director of personal banking and small business at Danske Bank, said the discretionary wealth business ‘has been a good part of our business for many years' with assets under management of around £500 million.

He added: ‘However, after a strategic review looking at anticipated future costs and regulatory change, it became clear that the best way forward for our customers was to have support in this area from a specialist wealth management company.

‘We are delighted to have found in Davy a locally-based, leading national wealth business that has a track record of strong delivery for customers.'

Stephen Felle (pictured), UK chief executive of Davy, added: ‘The addition of Danske Bank's business gives us an opportunity to build long-term relationships with a new group of customers.

‘It also underpins Davy's position as the leading wealth manager in Northern Ireland and opens a new era of partnership between two leading financial institutions.'

HD Press Release: Danske Bank Plc Group's January - June 2017: Solid performance across businesses
WC 1183 words
PD 20 July 2017
ET 01:36
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

 
   Danske Bank Plc Group's January - June 2017: 
 
   Solid performance across businesses 
 
   Danske Bank Finland's* core business continued to perform solidly in 
January-June 2017. The Finnish economy grew faster than previously 
forecasted, and the Bank's lending increased to both personal and 
corporate customers. Lending to small and medium sized corporate 
customers increased by 6 %, with healthy demand across business sectors. 
Consumer interest in mortgages continued record high, and the volume of 
new granted mortgages grew by 13 % compared to previous year. 
 
   Total income for Danske Bank's operations in Finland for January - June 
2017 amounted to EUR 324.8 million (EUR 316.9 million in H1 2016), up 3 
% compared to previous year. The growth was mainly due to increase in 
net interest income. Operating expenses were flat, and profit before 
taxes increased by 6 % to EUR 138.7 million. 
 
   "During the first half of the year we saw continued solid performance 
across business units. Net interest income development is on a good 
track, driven by steady growth in lending in combination with lower 
funding costs" said Risto Tornivaara, CEO of Danske Bank Plc. 
 
 
 
   Mobile payments gained good traction during the period. MobilePay 
downloads increased with more than 50% to over 500.000. MobilePay's 
position as Finland's leading mobile payment solution was further 
strengthened by the launch of Finland's first small business mobile 
payment solution and new payment provider partnership agreements which 
brought MobilePay to over 10.000 online shops. 
 
   *Includes Danske Bank Plc Group and the Helsinki Branch of Danske Bank 
A/S. 
 
 
 
   Financial Highlights of Danske Bank's operations in Finland 
 
   In addition to Danske Bank Plc, Danske Bank's operations in Finland 
include the Helsinki branch of Danske Bank A/S.

   *Danske Bank Plc's profit after taxes for January-June is not included

   Figures in this press release have not been audited. 
 
   Danske Bank Plc publishes only one interim report during 2017. The 
entire report for January-June 2017 is attached to this release as a PDF 
file. The Group's financial statement for January-December 2017 will be 
released on 2 February 2018. 
 
   Outlook for 2017 
 
   Growth in Finnish economy is expected to remain moderate in 2017 - 2018 
and the interest environment, especially short-term interest rates, is 
expected to remain at low level also during H2 2017. 
 
   We expect our lending to personal and corporate customers to continue 
growing in 2017 and thus we anticipate that our net interest income and 
total income will be higher compared to 2016. 
 
   Operating expenses are expected to be slightly lower than previous year 
since the Bank continues to have a strong focus on improving our cost 
efficiency and operational processes. Overall, we expect that profit 
before tax for 2017 will be slightly higher than 2016. 
 
   Merging of activities in Finland 
 
   As described in Annual Report 2016, Danske Bank is taking steps to merge 
its Finnish banking activities into Danske Bank A/S, Helsinki branch. 
The merger is going according to plan, and Danske Bank has applied for 
the required approvals. The merger rationale is to simplify our 
organisation. The change will be primarily of a technical nature and 
would not change the way in which we serve our customers, nor would 
employees experience changes. 
 
 
 
   For further information: 
 
   Risto Tornivaara, CEO of Danske Bank Plc, tel. +358 (0)10 546 6675 
 
 
 
   Danske Bank is Finland's third largest bank, which serves around a 
million Finnish personal, business and institutional customers. Danske 
Bank Plc is a part of the Nordic Danske Bank Group. 
 
   Danske Bank is a Nordic universal bank with strong regional roots and 
bridges to the rest of the world. We serve more than 3.4 million 
personal, business and institutional customers, and in addition to 
banking services, we offer life insurance and pension, mortgage credit, 
wealth management, real estate and leasing services and products. 
 
 
 
   Our vision is to be recognised as the most trusted financial partner. We 
are driven by a desire to make important financial decisions and daily

and investors and the societies we are a part of.

HD H1 earnings of Danske Bank in Estonia grow 5 pct
WC 229 words
PD 20 July 2017
ET 03:20
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Baltic News Service

LP 

TALLINN, Jul 20, BNS – The profit of Danske Bank in Estonia in the first six months of 2017 was 6.1 million euros, 5 percent bigger than in the same period last year.

Operating income meanwhile dropped 14 percent year over year.

TD 

Ivar Pae, manager of the Estonian branch of Danske, said that profit for the period grew 5 percent thanks to an improvement in portfolio quality as a result of loan impairment reversals.

The bank's operating income fell 14 percent year over year to 9.1 million euros. Expenses decreased from 5.8 million to 5.7 million euros. The cost-income ratio in the first half-year was 62.6 percent, compared with 55 percent a year ago.

The net value of the loan portfolio grew by 9 million euros. Deposits declined by 421 million euros or 44 percent, as in the present negative interest rate environment raising funds from local customers is not attractive for the bank.

The bank did not book additional impairment charges in the first half of 2017 because the quality of the loan portfolio was very good. As at June 30, accumulated impairment charges amounted to seven million euros, and the ratio of impairments to loans was 0.8 percent.

Tallinn newsroom, +372 610 8826, majandus@bns.ee

Baltic News Service

HD Profit of Latvian branch of Danske Bank drops 17% in H1
WC 309 words
PD 20 July 2017
ET 03:58
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Baltic News Service

LP 

RIGA, Jul 20, BNS - Net profit of the Latvian branch of Danske Bank in the first half of this year was EUR 1.9 million, down 17 percent from the respective period last year, the bank reported.

The bank's profit before impairment charges was EUR 1.7 million in the first six months of 2017 or by 11 percent lower than in January-June 2016.

TD 

As a result of growing business volumes, total income rose 18 percent to EUR 4.7 million in the first half of 2017. Net interest income grew 24 percent to EUR 3.6 million. Net fee income stood at EUR 1 million, unchanged year-on-year.

The bank's expenses grew 43 percent compared to the first half of 2016, reaching EUR 3 million. Because of the sale of the bank’s retail business, a larger share of expenses is now allocated to the bank's core activities. Another reason was expenses related to the upcoming launch of a single platform for Baltic operations. The single platform will allow us to further improve internal processes, and thus the bank expects to see lower expense growth in the future.

The deposit portfolio rose 14 percent to EUR 369.3 million, with increases in deposits from both institutional and corporate customers.

The loan portfolio for core segment customers rose 28 percent to EUR 352.8 million. The loans in the said period amounted to EUR 104 million.

Danske Bank is committed to continuing to increase its business banking volume in Latvia, and pursue this goal by offering customers sophisticated advice and tailor-made financing solutions. The bank also focuses on the efficient use of capital in order to compete successfully and provide the best offerings to its customers.

BNS, +371 67088611, zinas@bns.lv

HD Danske Bank Lithuania's H1 net profit from core activities drops 39 pct to EUR 4 mln
WC 241 words
PD 20 July 2017
ET 03:59
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, Jul 20, BNS - Danske Bank, the second-biggest financial group in Northern Europe by assets, saw its first-half net profit from core activities of corporate and private banking in Lithuania drop by 39 percent to 4 million euros, down from 6.6 million euros in the same period last year.

Pretax earnings from core activities dropped by 24 percent to 4.8 million euros, according to the bank's first-half financial report.

TD 

"Increased operating expenses, negative interest rates as well as a decline in fee and net trading income were key factors for Danske Bank Lithuania's financial performance in the first half of 2017," Danske Bank Lithuania CEO Gintautas Galvanauskas said in a press release.

The Lithuanian branch's total income declined by 8 percent to 9.1 million euros, with net interest income down by 4 percent to 6.7 million euros, net fee income down by 11 percent to 1.6 million euros and net trading income down by 27 percent to 0.8 million euros.

Its operating expenses, meanwhile, grew by 21 percent to 5.8 million euros.

The branch's loan portfolio shrank by 3 percent over the year to 723 million euros, while its deposit portfolio grew by 21 percent to 999 million euros.

Vilnius newsroom, verslas@bns.lt, +370 5 205 8520

HD Gross profit of Danske Bank Lithuania H1 was EUR 4.8mn
WC 266 words
PD 21 July 2017
SN Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA
SC ELTA
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA

LP 

Vilnius, July 21 (ELTA) - In the first half of 2017, Danske Bank Lithuania's profit before tax for core activities was EUR 4.8 million (against EUR 6.3 million in H1 2016), the bank reports.

In H1, Danske Bank Lithuania's net interest income stood at EUR 6.7 million (against EUR 7 million a year ago). Operating expenses amounted to EUR 5.8 million (against EUR 4.8 million for the first half of 2016). The loan portfolio was EUR 723 million (against EUR 746 million a year ago), core activity deposit portfolio was EUR 999 million (against EUR 823 million for the first half of 2016).

TD 

"Bigger operating expenses, negative interest rates as well as a decline in fee and net trading income were key factors for Danske Bank Lithuania's financial performance in the first half of 2017. Operating expenses increased mainly due to investment in new customer servicing platform in Baltic countries which will eventually allow us to create additional value for our customers, optimise operating costs, and adjust to the new regulatory environment," says Gintautas Galvanauskas, the CEO of Danske Bank Lithuania.

Danske Bank's investment in single Baltic banking customer platform is a response to the need for business customers to have a single banking system in all Baltic States, which also would be integrated in Danske Bank group's system. Danske Bank already has a single customer service platform in Lithuania and Latvia. Project is planned to be completed in the first quarter of 2018.

SE Finance
HD Danske action over €8.2m described as ‘typical bullying tactics’
BY Mark Hilliard
WC 309 words
PD 22 July 2017
SN The Irish Times
SC IRTI
PG 16
LA English
CY (c) 2017, The Irish Times.

LP 

A bankruptcy action brought against Bill Cullen by Danske Bank has been criticised as "typical bullying tactics" against a customer suffering from serious illness, a spokesman for the former Apprentice host said.

Mr Cullen was issued with a bankruptcy petition which was heard briefly before the High Court this week before being adjourned.

TD 

It relates to an outstanding debt of €8.2 million owed to Danske Bank, which has been pursuing it since 2012.

Mr Cullen was not believed to have been in court for the hearing and is understood to be receiving treatment for a serious illness.

In response to the proceedings, a spokesman for the businessman told The Irish Times: "This is typical bullying tactics of Danske Bank using their dominant position to abuse a customer who is suffering from a serious illness, the nature of which they have been made fully aware.

"Mr Cullen will be taking all legal steps to protect his position."

Danske Bank declined to comment.

In the High Court in 2014, Mr Cullen opposed Danske's demand he sell his house to satisfy an €8.2 million judgment obtained against him in 2012. Danske had applied for a court order for the sale of Osberstown House in Naas, Co Kildare.

At that time the court heard Mr Cullen's wife, Rita Cullen, and his partner of 35 years, Jackie Lavin, were both opposing the application to force the sale.

In its claim, Danske said a judgment registered in November 2012 against Mr Cullen for €8.21 million remained unpaid.

Mr Cullen was opposing the order for sale on grounds including that the bank has made inadequate efforts to ameliorate his debt through the proper marketing of two properties over which a receiver had been appointed. Danske denied those claims.

HD Press Release: Fitch Affirms Danske Bank AS's Mortgage Cover Pool I Covered Bonds at 'AAA'
WC 2326 words
PD 24 July 2017
ET 04:32
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

 
 
The following is a press release from Fitch Ratings:

Fitch Ratings-London-24 July 2017: Fitch Ratings has affirmed Danske Bank AS's (Danske, A/Stable/F1) mortgage covered bonds secured by the bank's cover pool I at 'AAA' with a Stable Outlook.

TD 

KEY RATING DRIVERS

- The covered bonds' rating is based on Danske's Long-Term Issuer Default Rating (IDR) of 'A' and the unchanged IDR uplift of two notches, payment continuity uplift (PCU) of five notches and recovery uplift of one notch. The 12.0% over-collateralisation (OC) that Fitch gives credit to and which is the lowest nominal OC of the last 12 months, provides more protection than the revised 10.0% 'AAA' breakeven OC for the programme. The latter supports a 'AA+' tested rating on a probability of default basis and a one-notch recovery uplift to 'AAA'. The Stable Outlook on the covered bonds' rating reflects a three-notch buffer against an issuer downgrade, due to the different uplift factors above the bank's IDR.

The 'AAA' breakeven OC is 10.0%, reduced from 10.5% previously. The updated results reflect the higher credit given to the assets' margins, in line with the agency's recently reviewed Norwegian residential mortgage rating criteria addendum and bespoke criteria for Danske Swedish mortgage loans. Due to the positive excess spread of the assets versus the covered bonds, the cash flow valuation component leads to a reduction of the 'AAA' breakeven OC by 6.0%, compared with 5.2% previously. Also, the credit loss component has decreased to 5.6% from 5.7%, due to a lower loan-to-value ratio for the assets. The asset disposal loss component of 10.3% reflects the large maturity mismatches between the assets and the liabilities (22.3 years weighted average residual life of the assets versus 4.3 years for the covered bonds). Fitch 'AAA' breakeven OC level for this programme anticipates a shift to a larger proportion of Norwegian assets in the pool.

As at 31 March 2017, the cover pool consisted of 63% Norwegian residential mortgages and 37% Swedish residential mortgages, reduced from 49% last year. The Swedish mortgages in Cover Pool I will be gradually transferred to a new Swedish mortgage institution. The Norwegian cover assets have a higher credit risk in Fitch's analysis and a lower margin than the Swedish cover assets. However, as the programme gradually becomes a pure Norwegian residential mortgage pool, we expect that the mismatches between the assets and liabilities will decrease. This is because the Norwegian cover assets are mostly amortising (67%) whereas the Swedish cover assets are mostly long-dated interest-only loans (68%) and the bonds denominated in SEK or swapped into SEK have a short weighted average residual maturity (three years).

The programme's two-notch IDR uplift reflects that covered bonds issued by a Danish universal bank are exempt from bail-in, Fitch's assessment that the risk of under-collateralisation at the point of resolution is sufficiently low, and that a resolution of Danske, should it happen, would not result in the direct enforcement of the recourse against the cover pool.

Fitch's PCU for the programme is five notches, lower than the standard six for mortgage covered bonds with a 12-month principal maturity extension and three-month protection for interest payment. This is due to the lack of formal provisions to find a refinancing solution without delay in the event of a maturity extension.

The recovery uplift for this programme is capped at one notch due to the presence of significant pre-swap FX mismatches between cover assets and liabilities. The FX covered bonds are fully hedged until maturity (including the extension period). However, upon a covered bonds' default, recoveries from SEK- and NOK-denominated assets, which have a longer WAL than the covered bonds, could expose holders of non SEK- and non NOK-denominated bonds to FX risk.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

- The 'AAA' rating would be vulnerable to downgrade if any of the following occurs: (i) the Issuer Default Rating (IDR) is downgraded by four notches to 'BBB-' or below; or (ii) the payment continuity uplift was reduced to one notch or less; or (iii) the level of overcollateralisation (OC) Fitch gives credit to fell below the 10% 'AAA' breakeven OC for the programme. If the actual OC was reduced to the issuer commitment of 2%, the covered bonds would be downgraded to 'AA', three notches above the bank's IDR.

The Fitch breakeven OC for the covered bond rating will be affected, among others, by the profile of the cover assets relative to outstanding covered bonds, which can change over time, even in the absence of new issuance. Therefore the breakeven OC to maintain the covered bond rating cannot be assumed to remain stable over time.

HD Sanitex raises EUR 23 million from Danske Bank
WC 338 words
PD 25 July 2017
ET 03:51
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Baltic News Service

LP 

RIGA, Jul 25, BNS - Sanitex, a wholesale and logistics services provider in the Baltic states, has concluded an agreement with Danske Bank on a credit facility and guarantee facility worth EUR 23 million, which the company will use to finance its working capital, BNS was told at the bank.

Sanitex board member Karlis Abele said that Danske Bank’s financing would provide stability to the company’s day-to-day operations and will help launch new, important projects, which in turn will enable Sanitex to reinforce its position in the industry.

TD 

Raivis Kakanis, the head of Danske Bank in Latvia, said that Sanitex is a company with a clear and well-planned growth vision and stable financial performance, and that its quality standards are high in all areas.

Sanitex, the Lithuanian-controlled wholesaler of household goods and food, closed 2016 with EUR 264.856 million in turnover, up 4.5 percent against a year before, while its profit shrank 2.1 times to EUR 647,062, according to information available at Firmas.lv.

The company’s wholesale revenue in Latvia grew by 4.4 percent to EUR 259.8 million last year, while export operations brought in EUR 5.056 million, up 8.2 percent year-on-year.

According to the company’s management, Sanitex successfully developed operations in the HoReCa (hotels, restaurants, cafes) segment, raising turnover by 20 percent. “This has been achieved thanks to an increase in the number of clients, as well as a significant growth of the product range,” the Sanitex management said in its report.

Sanitex closed 2015 with a EUR 1.369 million profit on EUR 253.414 million turnover.

Sanitex, founded in 1992, is operating in Lithuania and Latvia and is developing business in Estonia and Poland. The company provides logistics services not only to international companies, such as Philip Morris International, but also has its Cash & Carry stores. The group employs more than 3,500 people.

BNS, +371 67088611, zinas@bns.lv

HD Press Release: Extraordinary general meeting of Danske Bank Plc approved demerger of mortgage credit banking activities
WC 238 words
PD 31 July 2017
ET 08:17
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

 
 
 
 
  Company announcement      Danske Bank Plc 
                            31 July 2017 
 
 
   Extraordinary general meeting of Danske Bank Plc approved demerger of 
mortgage credit banking activities 
 
   Theextraordinary general meeting of Danske Bank Plc has approved the 
partial demerger in accordance with the demerger plan, first 
communicated on March 23, 2017, according to which Danske Bank Plc shall 
demerge by way of partial demerger so that all assets, liabilities and 
reserves of the mortgage credit banking business are transferred to one 
acquiring company, which will be called Danske Mortgage Bank Plc. 
 
   Establishing of the mortgage bank is a part of Danske Bank's plan to 
simplify its organization and legal structure and has no effect on 
Danske Bank's customers. The implementation of the partial demerger is 
still subject to regulatory approval and the aim is to establish the 
company during Autumn of 2017. 
 
   Danske Bank Plc 
 
   Contact: Anu Ilvonen, Head of MarCom in Danske Bank Plc, tel. +358 (0)10 
546 8002. 
 
   This announcement is distributed by Nasdaq Corporate Solutions on behalf 
of Nasdaq Corporate Solutions clients. 
 
   The issuer of this announcement warrants that they are solely 
responsible for the content, accuracy and originality of the information 
contained therein.

SoftBank Vision Fund, the more than $93 billion technology fund controlled by Japanese telecommunications giant SoftBank Group Corp., hired a senior investment banker from the ranks of Goldman Sachs Group Inc. Michael Ronen, co-chief operating officer of Goldman Sachs's global technology, media and telecommunications group, is joining the investment fund. Mr. Ronen started at Goldman Sachs as an associate in the communications, media and entertainment group in 1998 and was made a partner in 2012.

TD 

The two investment chiefs who led the private-equity arm of Danske Bank A/S have stepped down following an internal reorganization of the bank's asset management and private-equity platforms. John Danielsen and Peter Thellufsen, previously managing partner and senior partner, respectively, at Danske, left the fund-of-funds investor after the Danish bank "decided to integrate Danske Private Equity more closely into Danske Bank Asset Management," according to a statement.

Trident Capital Cybersecurity, a firm focused on early-stage investments, hired Ken Gonzalez as its fourth managing director. Mr. Gonzalez previously was a senior vice president at FireEye Inc., where he focused on corporate development. Although he has closed 23 cybersecurity acquisitions throughout his career, the new position represents his first job in venture capital.

Consumer-focused investor Brentwood Associates hired Craig Milius as a managing director. Earlier in his career, Mr. Milius was a general partner at growth-equity firm Austin Ventures, where he worked for 11 years and held positions on the firm's investment and operating committees. Before that, he worked as an investment professional with Cleveland private-equity firm Primus Capital.

Clearlake Capital Group brought on Xavier Gutierrez and Patrick Gilligan as managing directors. Mr. Gutierrez previously was chief investment officer of diversified holding company Meruelo Group, and Mr. Gilligan was a managing director at Park Hill Group, the placement-agent division of PJT Partners.

The Public Sector Pension Investment Board, one of Canada's largest pension funds, hired Marco Strizzi as an investment manager in its private-equity team. Mr. Strizzi joined PSP from European buyout firm BC Partners.

The Institutional Limited Partners Association said Mike Mazzola will take on the role of interim chief executive officer as the trade group searches for a permanent CEO. Mr. Mazzola replaces Peter Freire, who left ILPA in June. Mr. Mazzola recently retired from MetLife Inc. as senior vice president and head of alternative investments.

Christopher Hooper rejoined Welsh Carson Anderson & Stowe as a general partner. Mr. Hooper, who previously spent seven years with the firm, moved in 2011 to San Francisco, where he worked for Golden Gate Capital focusing on technology deals. He now is a member of Welsh Carson's tech team in San Francisco.

Infrastructure investment firm Global Infrastructure Partners appointed Jennifer Powers as a partner and chairwoman of its credit business. Ms. Powers, who will join the firm in September, will work to expand the firm's credit business, which provides financing for infrastructure assets and projects. She previously co-led Mizuho Bank Ltd.'s investment-grade debt-capital markets activities.

VC ROUNDUP: Y Combinator added Gustaf Alströmer, formerly product leader of Airbnb Inc.'s growth team, as a partner, and Pebble Technology Corp. founder Eric Migicovsky, as a visiting partner...Agricultural-technology firm Finistere Ventures hired David Duncan as a venture partner. Mr. Duncan has led a number of agricultural businesses, including FBSciences Inc.

LBO ROUNDUP: KKR & Co. executive Paul Horwood was appointed European chief financial officer at the firm. Mr. Horwood takes over the position from Peter Liu, who has stepped into the role of CFO for the Asia-Pacific region...Ashley Ciaburri Rainwater joined Comvest Partners as director of investor relations. She most recently worked at Kohlberg & Co. as director of marketing and investor relations...TSG Consumer Partners hired Jessica Duran from Deloitte LLP as chief financial officer, chief compliance officer and managing director...General Atlantic appointed Yong Hak Huh as a special adviser to support the firm's initiatives in Asia. Mr. Huh previously founded consulting firm First Bridge Strategy Ltd....Thomas Chadwick, previously an associate with Madison Dearborn Partners, joined Pritzker Group's private-capital arm as a vice president on its manufactured products team...Three Hills Capital Partners added Joe Jefferies, Arjan Blok and Ravi Savjani as investment manager, senior associate and investor-relations manager, respectively...Mid Europa Partners appointed Alain Beyens, an executive who has worked with several private equity-backed companies, as an operating partner.

HD *Fitch Affirms Danske Bank and Realkredit Danmark at 'A'; Outlook Stable
WC 3098 words
PD 9 August 2017
ET 10:08
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

9 Aug 2017 10:08 ET Press Release: Fitch Affirms Danske Bank and Realkredit Danmark at 'A'; Outlook Stable

 
 
The following is a press release from Fitch Ratings:

TD 

Fitch Ratings-London-09 August 2017: Fitch Ratings has affirmed Danske Bank's (Danske) and its mortgage bank subsidiary Realkredit Danmark's (Realkredit) Long-Term Issuer Default Ratings (IDRs) at 'A', Short-Term IDRs at 'F1', and Viability Ratings (VRs) at 'a'. The Outlooks on the Long-Term IDRs are Stable.

In addition, Fitch has assigned Danske a 'A(dcr)' Derivative Counterparty Rating (DCR) as part of its roll-out of DCRs to significant derivative counterparties in Western Europe and the US. DCRs are issuer ratings and express Fitch's view of banks' relative vulnerability to default under derivative contracts with third-party, non-government counterparties.

A full list of rating actions is at the end of this rating action commentary.

The rating actions are part of a periodic portfolio review of two major Danish banking groups rated by Fitch.

KEY RATING DRIVERS

- DANSKE'S IDRS, DCR, VR AND SENIOR DEBT

- Danske's ratings reflects the bank's strong universal Danish and to a lesser extent, pan-Nordic franchise. This provides stable revenue generation across a wide range of products. The ratings also consider the bank's strong capitalisation as well as healthy funding and liquidity, although wholesale funding reliance makes the bank sensitive to a loss of investor confidence. We view positively management's renewed strategic focus on relationship banking in the Nordics.

The bank has taken steps to strengthen its risk management framework, and we expect this to translate into some further asset quality improvements. The stock of non-performing loans continues to decline on the back of a domestic economic recovery, enhanced underwriting standards and ongoing wind-down of the non-core Irish portfolio, which is no longer a material risk to the bank. It represented 2.3% of gross loans at end-June 2017, as calculated by Fitch, excluding loans that are fully collateralised.

Profitability metrics have improved, primarily as a result of lower loan impairment charges (LICs). The bank benefits from strong and stable revenue generation as well as good cost control. Margins have proven resilient to negative interest rates. For mortgage financing (mainly through Realkredit), Danske earns a fixed margin because the market interest rate on the covered bonds is passed through to the borrower. The bank's current loan loss reversals are clearly not sustainable, but we expect LICs to remain low. We also expect Danske's profitability to gradually benefit from its continued expansion in Norway and Sweden.

Danske has strong funding and liquidity. It is reliant on wholesale funding, like most Nordic banks, but its market access has proven highly resilient and it has a well-diversified funding base. Its mortgage business (via Realkredit) is by law entirely wholesale-funded by mortgage bonds that match the interest term of the underlying mortgage loan, and the duration of the issued mortgage bond portfolio has been extended in recent years through active reduction of short-term (up to two years) bonds. Fitch expects continued strong demand for Danish mortgage bonds in light of the need for domestic financial institutions, insurance companies and pension funds to hold highly liquid, high quality, securities in domestic currency. This is reinforced by a fairly limited outstanding volume of Danish government bonds. Nonetheless, maintaining a significant liquidity portfolio to mitigate refinancing risk is key for Danske's ratings.

Danske's risk-weighted capital ratios compare well with international peers, with a Fitch core capital ratio of 16.5% at end-June 2017. Leverage is somewhat high compared with peers, although still acceptable, with a reported fully loaded Basel III ratio of 4.1%.

We have assigned Danske a DCR due to its significant derivatives activity. The DCR is at the same level as the Long-Term IDR because under Danish legislation, derivative counterparties have no preferential status over other senior obligations in a resolution scenario.

REALKREDIT'S IDRS, VR AND SENIOR DEBT

- Realkredit's ratings reflect its strong domestic franchise as the second-largest mortgage lender, its strong capitalisation and its resilient asset quality. The ratings are constrained by the bank's monoline business model and wholesale funding reliance, although risks associated with the latter are mitigated by a large, deep and liquid domestic covered bond market, and access to funding from its parent if needed.

Realkredit's ratings are based on its standalone financial strength, despite the sharing of some central functions and distribution channels with its parent bank. Fitch also expects capital is fungible between Danske and Realkredit to a significant extent, and thus Fitch is likely to retain the VRs within one notch of each other.

Realkredit's assets represent the majority of Danske's mortgage loan exposure. Fitch expects the quality of this portfolio to remain strong, supported by a stabilising Danish economy. We expect profitability to remain low but stable, underpinned by resilient revenue generation, tight cost control and a continued focus on underwriting.

Realkredit is by law entirely wholesale-funded, largely through issuance of Danish mortgage bonds. Similar to its domestic peers, about 20% of Realkredit's bonds mature within a year to match the duration of the bank's underlying mortgage loans. Short-term bonds have fallen to less than 10% of Realkredit's total stock of mortgage bonds, and recent price adjustments will help reduce those volumes somewhat further. The supportive dynamics of the Danish mortgage bond market and Denmark's law on mortgage bond maturity extensions reduces refinancing risks.

Realkredit's risk-weighted capital ratios compare strongly with those of domestic and international peers, although boosted by relatively low risk weights on mortgage loans. Leverage is good in a European context.

SUPPORT RATING AND SUPPORT RATING FLOOR

- Danske's Support Rating (SR) of '5' and Support Rating Floor (SRF) of 'No Floor' reflect Fitch's view that senior creditors cannot rely on receiving full extraordinary support from the sovereign in the event of it becoming non-viable. The EU's Bank Recovery and Resolution Directive (BRRD) provides a framework for resolving banks that is likely to require senior creditors participating in losses, if necessary, instead of or ahead of a bank receiving sovereign support.

Realkredit's SR of '1' reflects an extremely high probably that support would be provided by Danske, if required. In Fitch's view, Danske would have high propensity to support Realkredit given the latter's role as the group's main domestic mortgage provider, and the significant reputational risk Danske would face in the event of a default of Realkredit. Any required support would likely be manageable relative to Danske's ability to provide it.

SUBORDINATED DEBT AND OTHER HYBRID SECURITIES

- Subordinated debt and other hybrid capital issued by Danske are all notched down from the bank's VR and have been affirmed accordingly.

In accordance with Fitch's criteria, subordinated debt and CRD IV-compliant Tier 2 instruments are rated one notch below Danske's VR to reflect the above-average loss severity of this type of debt relative to average recoveries. The narrow notching partly reflects the absence of contractual full write-down or conversion language.

Fitch rates Danske's other Tier 2 instruments three notches below the VR to reflect loss severity (one notch) and incremental non-performance risk (two notches). Of the latter, compared with new CRD IV-compliant Tier 2 notes, Fitch has applied an additional single notch for incremental non-performance risk to legacy issues because of the issuer's ability to defer coupons. The ability to defer interest is the differentiation between the old-style Tier 2 instruments and the new CRD IV-compliant Tier 2 notes

Tier 1 instruments and Additional Tier securities are rated four and five notches below Danske's VR, respectively, to reflect the higher than average loss severity risk of these securities (two notches) as well as high risk of non-performance (an additional two and three notches, respectively).

RATING SENSITIVITIES

- DANSKE'S IDRS, VR AND SENIOR DEBT

- A sustained and material improvement in asset quality and profitability metrics could result in positive rating pressure in the medium term. This would also require management to successfully execute its current strategy, with a clear focus on Nordic home markets, while maintaining solid capital, funding and liquidity ratios.

While unexpected, a downgrade could also result from a prolonged inability to competitively access debt capital markets, if the Danish business faces a significant asset quality deterioration that materially impacts capitalisation or if the improving earnings trend reverses. At the current rating, Fitch expects Danske to maintain a large liquidity buffer and minimise maturity gaps to mitigate funding risks.

REALKREDIT'S IDRS, VR AND SENIOR DEBT

- The Stable Outlook reflects both Fitch's view that Realkredit will maintain its focus on asset quality and continue to generate capital internally, and the Stable Outlook on Danske Bank. A VR upgrade for Realkredit is unlikely given its already high ratings for a monoline business model. An upgrade of Danske Bank's IDRs would likely result in an upgrade of Realkredit's IDRs, at which point Realkredit's IDRs would be driven by parent support.

A downgrade of Realkredit would most likely be a result of it being unable to competitively access wholesale funding markets or if it significantly increases its reliance on international debt investors, who may prove less stable during financial stress. A downgrade of Danske's ratings, or reduced focus on liquidity, would also be rating negative.

SUPPORT RATING AND SUPPORT RATING FLOOR

9 Aug 2017 10:08 ET Press Release: Fitch Affirms Danske Bank and -2-

- An upgrade of Danske's SR or upward revision of the SRF would be contingent on a positive change in Denmark's propensity to support its banks. While not impossible, this is highly unlikely, in Fitch's view.

Realkredit's SR of '1' is sensitive to any perceived change in Danske's propensity or ability to provide support.

SUBORDINATED DEBT AND OTHER HYBRID SECURITIES

- As subordinated debt and other hybrid securities are notched down from Danske's VR, their respective ratings are sensitive to a change in Danske's VR. They are also sensitive to Fitch changing its assessment of the probability of their non-performance risk relative to the risk captured in Danske's VR.

-

HD Fitch Affirms Danske Bank and Realkredit Danmark at 'A'; Outlook Stable
WC 3059 words
PD 9 August 2017
ET 10:08
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2017 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

(The following statement was released by the rating agency) LONDON, August 09 (Fitch) Fitch Ratings has affirmed Danske Bank's (Danske) and its mortgage bank subsidiary Realkredit Danmark's (Realkredit) Long-Term Issuer Default Ratings (IDRs) at 'A', Short-Term IDRs at 'F1', and Viability Ratings (VRs) at 'a'. The Outlooks on the Long-Term IDRs are Stable. In addition, Fitch has assigned Danske a 'A(dcr)' Derivative Counterparty Rating (DCR) as part of its roll-out of DCRs to significant derivative counterparties in Western Europe and the US. DCRs are issuer ratings and express Fitch's view of banks' relative vulnerability to default under derivative contracts with third-party, non-government counterparties. A full list of rating actions is at the end of this rating action commentary. The rating actions are part of a periodic portfolio review of two major Danish banking groups rated by Fitch.

TD 

KEY RATING DRIVERS DANSKE'S IDRS, DCR, VR AND SENIOR DEBT Danske's ratings reflects the bank's strong universal Danish and to a lesser extent, pan-Nordic franchise. This provides stable revenue generation across a wide range of products. The ratings also consider the bank's strong capitalisation as well as healthy funding and liquidity, although wholesale funding reliance makes the bank sensitive to a loss of investor confidence. We view positively management's renewed strategic focus on relationship banking in the Nordics. The bank has taken steps to strengthen its risk management framework, and we expect this to translate into some further asset quality improvements. The stock of non-performing loans continues to decline on the back of a domestic economic recovery, enhanced underwriting standards and ongoing wind-down of the non-core Irish portfolio, which is no longer a material risk to the bank. It represented 2.3% of gross loans at end-June 2017, as calculated by Fitch, excluding loans that are fully collateralised. Profitability metrics have improved, primarily as a result of lower loan impairment charges (LICs). The bank benefits from strong and stable revenue generation as well as good cost control. Margins have proven resilient to negative interest rates. For mortgage financing (mainly through Realkredit), Danske earns a fixed margin because the market interest rate on the covered bonds is passed through to the borrower. The bank's current loan loss reversals are clearly not sustainable, but we expect LICs to remain low. We also expect Danske's profitability to gradually benefit from its continued expansion in Norway and Sweden. Danske has strong funding and liquidity. It is reliant on wholesale funding, like most Nordic banks, but its market access has proven highly resilient and it has a well-diversified funding base. Its mortgage business (via Realkredit) is by law entirely wholesale-funded by mortgage bonds that match the interest term of the underlying mortgage loan, and the duration of the issued mortgage bond portfolio has been extended in recent years through active reduction of short-term (up to two years) bonds. Fitch expects continued strong demand for Danish mortgage bonds in light of the need for domestic financial institutions, insurance companies and pension funds to hold highly liquid, high quality, securities in domestic currency. This is reinforced by a fairly limited outstanding volume of Danish government bonds. Nonetheless, maintaining a significant liquidity portfolio to mitigate refinancing risk is key for Danske's ratings. Danske's risk-weighted capital ratios compare well with international peers, with a Fitch core capital ratio of 16.5% at end-June 2017. Leverage is somewhat high compared with peers, although still acceptable, with a reported fully loaded Basel III ratio of 4.1%. We have assigned Danske a DCR due to its significant derivatives activity. The DCR is at the same level as the Long-Term IDR because under Danish legislation, derivative counterparties have no preferential status over other senior obligations in a resolution scenario. REALKREDIT'S IDRS, VR AND SENIOR DEBT Realkredit's ratings reflect its strong domestic franchise as the second-largest mortgage lender, its strong capitalisation and its resilient asset quality. The ratings are constrained by the bank's monoline business model and wholesale funding reliance, although risks associated with the latter are mitigated by a large, deep and liquid domestic covered bond market, and access to funding from its parent if needed. Realkredit's ratings are based on its standalone financial strength, despite the sharing of some central functions and distribution channels with its parent bank. Fitch also expects capital is fungible between Danske and Realkredit to a significant extent, and thus Fitch is likely to retain the VRs within one notch of each other. Realkredit's assets represent the majority of Danske's mortgage loan exposure. Fitch expects the quality of this portfolio to remain strong, supported by a stabilising Danish economy. We expect profitability to remain low but stable, underpinned by resilient revenue generation, tight cost control and a continued focus on underwriting. Realkredit is by law entirely wholesale-funded, largely through issuance of Danish mortgage bonds. Similar to its domestic peers, about 20% of Realkredit's bonds mature within a year to match the duration of the bank's underlying mortgage loans. Short-term bonds have fallen to less than 10% of Realkredit's total stock of mortgage bonds, and recent price adjustments will help reduce those volumes somewhat further. The supportive dynamics of the Danish mortgage bond market and Denmark's law on mortgage bond maturity extensions reduces refinancing risks. Realkredit's risk-weighted capital ratios compare strongly with those of domestic and international peers, although boosted by relatively low risk weights on mortgage loans. Leverage is good in a European context. SUPPORT RATING AND SUPPORT RATING FLOOR Danske's Support Rating (SR) of '5' and Support Rating Floor (SRF) of 'No Floor' reflect Fitch's view that senior creditors cannot rely on receiving full extraordinary support from the sovereign in the event of it becoming non-viable. The EU's Bank Recovery and Resolution Directive (BRRD) provides a framework for resolving banks that is likely to require senior creditors participating in losses, if necessary, instead of or ahead of a bank receiving sovereign support. Realkredit's SR of '1' reflects an extremely high probably that support would be provided by Danske, if required. In Fitch's view, Danske would have high propensity to support Realkredit given the latter's role as the group's main domestic mortgage provider, and the significant reputational risk Danske would face in the event of a default of Realkredit. Any required support would likely be manageable relative to Danske's ability to provide it. SUBORDINATED DEBT AND OTHER HYBRID SECURITIES Subordinated debt and other hybrid capital issued by Danske are all notched down from the bank's VR and have been affirmed accordingly. In accordance with Fitch's criteria, subordinated debt and CRD IV-compliant Tier 2 instruments are rated one notch below Danske's VR to reflect the above-average loss severity of this type of debt relative to average recoveries. The narrow notching partly reflects the absence of contractual full write-down or conversion language. Fitch rates Danske's other Tier 2 instruments three notches below the VR to reflect loss severity (one notch) and incremental non-performance risk (two notches). Of the latter, compared with new CRD IV-compliant Tier 2 notes, Fitch has applied an additional single notch for incremental non-performance risk to legacy issues because of the issuer's ability to defer coupons. The ability to defer interest is the differentiation between the old-style Tier 2 instruments and the new CRD IV-compliant Tier 2 notes Tier 1 instruments and Additional Tier securities are rated four and five notches below Danske's VR, respectively, to reflect the higher than average loss severity risk of these securities (two notches) as well as high risk of non-performance (an additional two and three notches, respectively). RATING SENSITIVITIES DANSKE'S IDRS, VR AND SENIOR DEBT A sustained and material improvement in asset quality and profitability metrics could result in positive rating pressure in the medium term. This would also require management to successfully execute its current strategy, with a clear focus on Nordic home markets, while maintaining solid capital, funding and liquidity ratios. While unexpected, a downgrade could also result from a prolonged inability to competitively access debt capital markets, if the Danish business faces a significant asset quality deterioration that materially impacts capitalisation or if the improving earnings trend reverses. At the current rating, Fitch expects Danske to maintain a large liquidity buffer and minimise maturity gaps to mitigate funding risks. REALKREDIT'S IDRS, VR AND SENIOR DEBT The Stable Outlook reflects both Fitch's view that Realkredit will maintain its focus on asset quality and continue to generate capital internally, and the Stable Outlook on Danske Bank. A VR upgrade for Realkredit is unlikely given its already high ratings for a monoline business model. An upgrade of Danske Bank's IDRs would likely result in an upgrade of Realkredit's IDRs, at which point Realkredit's IDRs would be driven by parent support. A downgrade of Realkredit would most likely be a result of it being unable to competitively access wholesale funding markets or if it significantly increases its reliance on international debt investors, who may prove less stable during financial stress. A downgrade of Danske's ratings, or reduced focus on liquidity, would also be rating negative. SUPPORT RATING AND SUPPORT RATING FLOOR An upgrade of Danske's SR or upward revision of the SRF would be contingent on a positive change in Denmark's propensity to support its banks. While not impossible, this is highly unlikely, in Fitch's view. Realkredit's SR of '1' is sensitive to any perceived change in Danske's propensity or ability to provide support. SUBORDINATED DEBT AND OTHER HYBRID SECURITIES As subordinated debt and other hybrid securities are notched down from Danske's VR, their respective ratings are sensitive to a change in Danske's VR. They are also sensitive to Fitch changing its assessment of the probability of their non-performance risk relative to the risk captured in Danske's VR. HD Angry Birds maker Rovio plans $400 million IPO; could value company at $2 billion
BY Bloomberg
WC 263 words
PD 14 August 2017
SN Financial Express
SC AIWFIE
LA English
CY Copyright 2017 Indian Express Online Media Pvt. Ltd.

LP 

Rovio Entertainment Oy is planning an initial public offering as early as next month that could value the maker of the Angry Birds mobile games and movie at about $2 billion, said people familiar with the matter.

Rovio could raise about $400 million from a local market listing, the people said, asking not to be identified as the details aren't public. No final decisions have been made and the company could also choose to stay private for longer, they said.

TD 

Carnegie Bank A/S, Danske Bank A/S and Deutsche Bank AG are among banks advising on a potential listing, the people said. Representatives for Rovio, Carnegie, Danske and Deutsche Bank declined to comment.

Rovio, based in Espoo, Finland, reported revenue growth of 34 percent for 2016 to 190.3 million euros ($225 million) and earnings before interests and taxes of about 17.5 million euros compared with a loss in the previous year. The company, like many game makers, has been searching for new growth after its initial success with the Angry Birds mobile game.

The company sold parts of its business to Kaiken Entertainment, a startup led by former Chief Executive Officer Mikael Hed and other company veterans, in March. The sale -- which included Rovio's TV animation studio, book publishing business and some non-Angry Birds properties-- was part of a reorganization at the company.

Rovio has been searching for new growth after its initial success with the Angry Birds mobile game. (Image: Reuters)[http://images.financialexpress.com/2017/08/angry-birds-reuters.jpg]

HD Biciulaitis to take over as Danske Bank Lithuania CEO from Galvanauskas
WC 160 words
PD 4 September 2017
ET 05:26
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, Sep 04, BNS - Danske Bank Lithuania CEO Gintautas Galvanauskas in early October will leave the bank he has headed for 17 years and will be replaced by Ramunas Biciulaitis, the bank's current CFO.

"Although I intend to remain active in business, I want changes and new activities and to be able to have more time for myself and my family," Galvanauskas, 60, said in a press release on Monday.

TD 

Galvanauskas started as CEO of Sampo Lithuania back in 2001 and remained in the post after Danske Bank purchased the bank from Finland's Sampo in 2008.

Biciulaitis has been with Danske Bank since 2009. Before that, he was a management board member and CFO at Leo LT, a company set up for a new nuclear power plant project, and, previously, CFO of the brewery Kalnapilis-Tauras.

Vilnius newsroom, verslas@bns.lt, +370 5 205 8511

HD Estonia: Danske Bank mediates millions of euros of Azerbaijani bribes
WC 304 words
PD 5 September 2017
ET 03:54
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Baltic News Service

LP 

TALLINN, Sep 05, BNS – The Estonian branch of Danske Bank through its accounts allowed for the mediation of millions of euros of bribe money from Azerbaijan to Europe, the daily Postimess writes in relation to the international journalistic investigation.

Last spring, Postimees wrote how from 2012-2014 transactions in the amount of approximately 2.5 billion dollars were made to Estonian banks by Azerbaijani firms. Investigation conducted by Danish daily Berlingske Tidende, Estonian Aripaev and many international media publications showed that the sum was even bigger, amounting to 2.9 billion dollars.

TD 

While at the end of the 2000s, a few dozen million dollars a year was transferred from Azerbaijan to non-residents in Estonia, then in 2012 the sum grew to approximately 800 million dollars and in 2013 to approximately 1.7 billion dollars.

From Estonia transactions were made from accounts of businesses registered in the United Kingdom, the owners of which find solace in the tax havens of Marshall Islands, Belize and British Virgin Islands. Representatives of the companies, who formalized opening the accounts with Danske Bank in Estonia, were Azerbaijanis living in Baku, while they weren't the actual beneficiaries of the firms.

Investigation shows that the sums were transferred within a time frame of two and a half years through a bank account created at the Estonian branch of Danske Bank to at least two European politicians, to a journalist who wrote regime friendly articles and to companies selling luxury goods, local prominent Azerbaijanis as well as to companies with hidden owners.

According to the investigation, German politician Eduard Lintner, board director of European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD) Kalin Mitrev and former producer at CNN Eckart Sager.

Tallinn newsroom, +372 610 8815, majandus@bns.ee

Baltic News Service

HD  Danske Bank forecasts 3.8 pct economic growth for Lithuania in 2017
WC 424 words
PD 5 September 2017
SN Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA
SC ELTA
LA English
CY (c) 2017 Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA

LP 

Vilnius, September 5 (ELTA) - Danske Bank has revised Lithuania's economic growth rate taking into account increasing exports, investments and domestic consumption. Danske Bank forecasts that Lithuania's economic growth will stand at 3.8 percent in 2017 (the highest figure since 2012), at 3.5 percent in 2018 and at 3.4 percent in 2019.

Chief Baltic Economist at Danske Bank Rokas Grajauskas says that there is greater certainty in 2017 compared to recent years. As prices of raw materials are recovering or have stabilised, emerging economies like Brazil and Russia show increasingly clearer signs of recovery, whereas China and India are increasing their imports. These countries buy more goods from the West which is one of the main reasons behind economic growth in the euro area and the Nordic Countries. This also affects Lithuania - as Western Europe exports more to emerging markets, Lithuania's export to Western Europe is growing as well.

TD 

Grajauskas notes that Lithuania's economy is directly dependent on Russia, one of emerging markets. It still remains an important trading partner as Lithuania exports 14 percent of all goods to Russia. Lithuania's export to Russia has increased by a third due to recovery in Russia.

Moreover, not only exports but investments are growing. This is noticeable in Central and Eastern Europe, the euro area and the Nordic countries. The decrease of investments was more noticeable in Estonia and Latvia last year, but this year it has recovered and increased by 17 percent. In Lithuania, investment growth stood at 7 percent in 2017 so far.

According to Grajauskas, domestic consumption is growing rapidly, too. Consumption is on the rise together with wages. Although consumption is lower compared to 2016 due to inflation, it nonetheless rose by 3-4 percent.

The economist says that all of the aforementioned factors create favourable conditions for fast economic growth and thus Danske Bank has revised Lithuania's economic growth forecast for 2017 from 3.1 percent (in November 2016) to 3.8 percent. This is the highest growth rate since 2012. Lithuania's economic growth should be high for several years to come because of recovering economies of Europe, the United States and emerging markets as well as due to the absorption of EU funds and growing wages resulting from improving financial situation of companies and shortage of employees. Danske Bank Forecasts that Lithuania's economy will grow by 3.5 percent in 2018 and by 3.4 percent in 2019.

Karolis Broga

HD  Danske Bank hires former head of intelligence agency to fight money laundering
WC 231 words

SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2017 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, Sept 5 (Reuters) - Danske Bank has hired the former head of Denmark's intelligence agency and fraud squad to help it in its effort to counter money laundering.

The announcement came on Tuesday after media reports that the bank's Estonian branch had been exploited for money laundering and other illegal activities between 2012 and 2014.

TD 

The bank said it was cooperating with authorities over the incidents. It had previously established that it in the period leading up to 2014 had had inadequate measures in place in Estonia to prevent money laundering, the bank said in an email to Reuters.

Jens Madsen, currently working in the Danish Foreign Ministry fighting terrorism financing, will be responsible for the bank's Compliance Incident Management handling the investigation of incidents where regulations and internal guidelines have possibly not been followed. He was formerly the head of the country's intelligence agency and its fraud squad.

"The hiring should be seen as part of the overall armament in the compliance area in Danske Bank, and it is clear that the first task will be to contribute to investigating the situation in Estonia before 2014," head of Danske Bank's Group Compliance Anders Meinert said in an e-mail to Reuters. (Reporting by Teis Jensen, editing by Louise)

SE Pro Private Markets
HD Nordic Capital Buys Swedish Fund Management Platform MFEX
BY By Joice Alves
WC 337 words
PD 7 September 2017
ET 11:22
SN WSJ Pro Private Equity
SC RSTPROPE
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

Nordic Capital, a Stockholm-based buyout firm, has bought MFEX Mutual Funds Exchange AB, a Swedish company that runs a fund management platform.

The cash for the purchase of a 70% stake came from Nordic Capital's €3.5 billion eighth buyout fund, which closed in 2013, the firm said in a statement.

TD 

The Stockholm-based fund distribution platform has €72 billion ($86.46 billion) of assets under under administration and operates in Europe and Asia.

The management and a number of existing shareholders will hold the remaining 30% of the company, according to a source.

Financial details on the deal were not disclosed. Nordic Capital said it is injecting "substantial equity" into MFEX.

Nordic Capital said it has been following MFEX for "some years." MFEX approached the private-equity firm in the spring of 2017 to explore a potential transaction that could fund the company's growth plans, which include organic growth, strategic partnerships and acquisitions, according to a person familiar with the

MFEX was founded in 1999 and has offices in Paris, Geneva, Singapore and Umeå, Sweden. It provides infrastructure for mutual fund distribution, connecting over 800 fund companies to over 100 distributors including Société Générale SA, Nordea Bank AB, Pictet Group, Danske Bank AS, Citigroup Inc., Edmond de Rothschild Group and Bank of Singapore.

The deal is Nordic Capital's sixth platform investment since the beginning of 2016, the firm said.

Nordic's recent activity in the financial services sector includes the €1.5 billion sale of Bambora Group AB, a payment technology company, to Ingenico Group in July. It also listed Resurs Holding AB, a consumer financing business, on Nasdaq in April 2016.

Other recent private-equity deals in the fund platform space include the €1.8 billion acquisition in March of Spanish platform Allfunds Bank SA by Hellman & Friedman and Singapore's sovereign wealth fund GIC Pte. Ltd.

SE THE MONDAY INTERVIEW
HD Europe's gentleman activist defends his territory; The Monday Interview: Christer Gardell, Founder, Cevian Capital
BY By Richard Milne
WC 1103 words
PD 11 September 2017
SN Financial Times
SC FTFTA
ED London Ed1
PG 24
LA English
CY Copyright 2017 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web.

LP 

He leads the region's biggest activist fund and faces formidable competition, as Richard Milne discovers

He is dressed in the Swedish business-casual outfit of jumper and shirt. He is softly spoken and is not inclined to send angry letters to chief executives. In short, Christer Gardell does not behave like the stereotypical activist investor.

TD 

But Mr Gardell, co-founder of Cevian Capital, is Europe's biggest activist - and one of the most influential in the world. He has shaken up boardrooms across the continent, taking aim at companies from Ericsson to Danske Bank and ThyssenKrupp to ABB, forcing them to make often radical changes.

He is mild-mannered compared with his US counterparts, such as Carl Icahn and Dan Loeb . Yet Mr Gardell is more committed than ever to the cause of activism. He argues that the rise of index funds owning more and more of companies could destroy capitalism.

"We are probably in a period where we will have more activism in Europe. Frankly, in an environment where passive index funds have taken such big market share, it is welcome for capitalism," he says, sitting in his modest office in central Stockholm.

Cevian, which has about $15.5bn in assets under management, has had swaths of northern Europe to itself. But there are signs that Cevian's rivals in the US are looking to Europe. Mr Loeb recently made the biggest move of his career by buying $3.5bn of shares in Nestlé, the Swiss consumer goods group, while Elliott Advisors, another large US activist, has targeted Akzo Nobel , the Dutch chemicals company.

Mr Gardell says there are enough targets to go around. Strikingly, he argues one of the main reasons for the move is that Europe is more fertile territory than the US.

"Probably the most attractive country for shareholder protection is Sweden," he says. "I told Carl Icahn once about corporate governance standards in Europe and he replied: 'This must be the shareholder paradise'."

This is reflected in the contrasting styles of activism on either side of the Atlantic. Mr Gardell this year took a 5.6 per cent stake in Ericsson, the Swedish telecoms equipment maker, and immediately got a seat on the nomination committee. Such a position is key for Cevian, because it can influence who sits on the board. A few weeks later, one of Mr Gardell's main targets - Leif Johansson, the chairman - stepped down without Cevian having to make much in the way of public statements.

In the US, by contrast, corporate governance is often protective of management, meaning shareholders have to make noise. Mr Gardell says: "They have to take a more aggressive approach. It's not a style; it's more a product of the US corporate governance approach. We see them come into Europe with a less shouty approach."

Mr Gardell set up Cevian 15 years ago with Lars Förberg, a former private equity executive whom he first met in the 1990s. Initially, they focused on Scandinavia. For the past decade Cevian has widened its horizons to Germany, Switzerland and the UK.

Wherever it invests, the approach is the same. Cevian buys stakes of between 5 and 20 per cent in companies it believes to be undervalued, holding its shares for about five to seven years. It then works with boards to unlock what it sees as the hidden value in the company, often by splitting the group up.

It often does this by encouraging change at board and management level. Mr Gardell points to Volvo Group, the Swedish truckmaker, where it swapped out most directors and the chief executive. Some businesses were sold off and the company focused on its core trucks business. "It sounds simple: the focus is to improve the businesses," he says.

Mr Gardell says he sees no reason to go in the opposite direction to the US as there are plenty of opportunities still in Europe. As well as the $1bn Ericsson stake, two more companies are being targeted, one that Cevian is close to disclosing and the other in which it has just started building a stake, he says.

It is a patient game. Mr Gardell says Cevian had Ericsson under observation for a decade before moving when shares became cheap. Returns for investors have been above average, with Cevian making a total 19.4 per cent last year.

But there have been hiccups, most prominently in its investment in Bilfinger, a German construction group. Mr Gardell says the 29.5 per cent stake - its first investment in Germany - was "a mistake" because Cevian failed to do a thorough analysis. It underestimated the problems of the deals that had built Bilfinger. "If it had been in Sweden we would have known we should have been careful. It was a lesson learnt to get into a new market," he adds. Cevian retains its stake in the company.

It has not stopped Cevian from going into other, seemingly more complicated, situations in Germany such as ThyssenKrupp, the highly traditional steel-to-elevators conglomerate in which it owns a 15.1 per cent stake. Mr Gardell says its corporate governance may not be as straightforward as at Scandinavian or British companies but that "the price level compensated for it".

Behind this is a belief that activism is a "relatively local" business. "We need to know the people, have networks, have a corporate governance tradition we're comfortable with," he says. "In some markets, the language is important," he adds. "It explains why some US activists may struggle in Europe."

There are still fights closer to home, however. Mr Gardell is particularly vexed by the system of A and B shares in Sweden, which gives owners of A shares a bigger share of voting rights.

"It's very difficult to challenge incompetence," Mr Gardell says. In what could be his motto, he adds: "It's the basis of capitalism: if something isn't working, you should fix it."

Second opinion

The US counterpart

Carl Icahn, the US activist investor, says Mr Gardell is among the "top-five guys in the investment community" and "one of the smartest guys I know".

Mr Icahn was so impressed he invested his own money in Cevian's management company. "It is very rare I put that kind of money in with anyone - it was one of my better investments."

He thinks Cevian will not "lose sleep" over US activists coming to Europe. "There are plenty [of targets] to go around," Mr Icahn adds.

SE Economy
HD Quick Hits: Turkish Central Bank Seen Holding Rates Steady; ING sees a growing chance of a Bank of England rate rise in November after the latest U.K. inflation figures
BY By WSJ Staff
WC 1357 words
PD 12 September 2017
ET 17:53
SN WSJ Pro Central Banking
SC RSTPROCB
LA English
CY Copyright © 2017, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

Turkey's central bank isn't expected to change interest rates at its policy meeting Thursday, while the Bank of England could be more likely to raise rates this year after figures released Tuesday showed U.K. inflation accelerated sharply in August. Here are quick hits on central banking and related market views from around the world.

Turkish Central Bank Seen Holding Rates Steady

TD 

Turkey's central bank is expected to keep all interest rates steady at its monetary policy committee meeting Thursday, according to 10 economists surveyed by The Wall Street Journal. The central bank "is likely to keep all key rates on hold…The next move from the Bank, however, is likely to be a cut rather than a hike. We only expect this to materialize in December rather than October as we previously forecast," TD Securities says.

Yeliz Candemir

Chile's Central Bank Seen Leaving Policy Rate on Hold

Chile's central bank likely will leave its benchmark interest rate unchanged this week for the fourth consecutive month, according to a survey of economists. Almost 90% of the economists surveyed by the central bank expect the rate to stay steady, while a few analysts see cuts. The consensus among the economists is that there won't be any changes for at least a year. Earlier this year, the bank had cut the rate on concerns about slow economic growth. The central bank's board of directors meets Thursday.

Ryan Dube

Argentina Monthly Inflation Rate Pressures Central Bank

Argentina's stubbornly high inflation rate, which clocked in at 1.4% on the month in August, is raising pressure on the country's central bank. The bank now finds itself farther from its stated goal of capping inflation at 17% this year. Inflation would have to be under 1% each month for the rest of 2017 if the annual rate is to end the year at 20%. August's numbers show just how hard it is to fight inflation, especially in a country where powerful unions demand constant wage increases and where highly taxed domestic factories produce goods that cost far more than they do in other countries. President Mauricio Macri has promised to "gradually" overhaul the economy, but it looks like the central bank may achieve its goal even more gradually than expected.

Taos Turner

ING Sees Growing Chance of BOE Rate Rise in November

If Andrew Haldane, the chief economist at the Bank of England, votes in favor of an interest-rate increase this week, there would be a 50% chance the central bank is going to raise rates in November, according to ING. On Tuesday, after the U.K. consumer inflation data came in higher than expected and got closer to 3%, the possibility of a rate rise in two months' time rose to 30% from 20%, says Chris Turner from ING. The thing is that "for some Monetary Policy Committee officials, 3% inflation may be the implicit line in the sand, where the growth-inflation trade-off starts to tilt in favor of an earlier-than-anticipated withdrawal of the current emergency stimulus policy backdrop," ING says.

Olga Cotaga

Sterling Rally Suggests Expectations of BOE Reaction

Sterling's rally after U.K. inflation data suggests that the market is looking for a reaction at this week's Bank of England meeting, says Shilen Shah, strategist at Investec Wealth & Investment. The pound was up against both the euro and dollar Tuesday. "The BOE has shown patience with above target CPI [consumer-price index] prints; however, some reduction in the dovish bias and a move towards a more neutral or even a few hawkish comments is currently expected by the market," Mr. Shah says. The BOE releases a policy statement Thursday.

Georgi Kantchev

U.K. Inflation Jump Unlikely to Spark Interest-Rate Rise

Just over half the rise in the U.K.'s headline consumer-price index in August versus July can be attributed to imports, according to RBC Capital Markets economist Sam Hill. This is evidence that sterling weakness matters a lot for inflation. Consumer prices increased 2.9% year-over-year in August, up from 2.6% the month before and above analyst expectations, with analysts attributing the gain to higher fuel and clothing prices. This print will give the Bank of England's monetary policy committee, which meets this week, food for thought, though Mr. Hill says it is unlikely to make more members vote for a rate rise this time around.

Tasos Vossos

Ten-Year Gilts Could Underperform U.K. Curve Soon

Ten-year gilts look expensive compared with the rest of the U.K. government bond-yield curve but could start underperforming once the Bank of England's ongoing reinvestment round ends next week, RBC Capital Markets says. The broker attributes lofty valuations to the lack of available gilts for the BOE to buy around the 10-year maturity and that the short end of the curve prices in very little in terms of policy rate rises. Meanwhile, in a broad selloff after the end of BOE reinvestments, short-dated bond yields may stay anchored thanks to growth headwinds from Britain's proposed departure from the European Union. The BOE is reinvesting £10.1 billion ($13.3 billion) of maturing government bonds it held under its quantitative-easing program to keep the stock of gilt holdings constant at £435 billion.

Tasos Vossos

More Supply and Demand for Euro Corporate Bonds

The euro corporate bond market attracts more of everything in September: more supply, as companies issue new debt, and more demand, as the European Central Bank boosts its buying of corporate bonds. The ECB bought €1.77 billion ($2.12 billion) of corporate bonds last week, the highest volume since early July, according to Commerzbank. Meanwhile, euro supply continues Tuesday with Dutch retailer Ahold and the London Stock Exchange offering new bonds.

Tasos Vossos

ECB May Taper QE, But Not Corporate Bond Buys

Corporate bond investors shouldn't be too scared of the potential tapering of the European Central Bank's quantitative-easing program, as the share of corporate purchases may even rise, Danske Bank says. This echoes the views of some other credit analysts, such as those at Citi who recently said corporate purchases could remain close to current levels even if public-sector purchases are reduced in the first half of 2018. Analysts generally expect the ECB to announce the tapering of its €60-billion-a-month ($72 billion) QE program this year and implement it in 2018.

Tasos Vossos

ECB QE Reinvestment Pickup Comes at the Right Time

Reinvestment of maturing bonds that the European Central Bank holds under its quantitative-easing program is poised to pick up to €15 billion ($18 billion) a month next year, just as the ECB likely will be cutting down on new purchases, ING strategists say. For now, the reinvestment amount averages less than €5 billion a month, they add. The ECB must reinvest maturing bonds to prevent the natural shrinkage of its QE stock. Analysts generally expect the ECB to announce tapering this year and implement it in 2018.

Tasos Vossos

Italian Debt to Return to the Spotlight Sooner or Later

Italian government debt should return to the spotlight due to the combination of a gradual reduction of the European Central Bank's accommodative policy and a potentially divided coalition government after the next election, according to Barclays strategist Fabio Fois. Against this background, Italy may be seen as unable to achieve overhauls to boost productivity and growth and steadily reduce public debt, Mr. Fois adds. Italy's debt-to-gross domestic product ratio ended 2016 at 133%, according to data from Allianz, which expects it to decline to 126% by 2020. Italy is due to hold a general election by next May.

Tasos Vossos
